======================================================================
PAGE: Jakata
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Jakata
======================================================================

Malaz Isle
Quon Tali
Korel,
aka
Lands of Fist
See also:
Jakatas (currency)
Jakata
(also
Jakatakan
- see section below) was a city on the southwestern coast of
Malaz Island
which was known for its seafaring people, notably pirates. Jakata was referred to as
Jakatan
as well, but the name (in that form) was used only once in the
Malazan main series
by
Steven Erikson
(in "The Crippled God"),
but it was used several times in
Ian C. Esslemont
's "Night of Knives".
Beak
made a comment about the Jakata people having been the first on Malaz Island after the
Stormriders
retreated.
The city was located where the
River Broland
exited into the strait known as the
Inside Passage
.  On the other side of the strait was a chain of islands which included
Break Island
.  Upriver from Jakata was the town known as
Upper Jakata
.
It is unknown if the Malazan Empire coinage known as a
Jakata
originated or was named after the city of the same name.
Jakata was believed to have begun as a
Napan
colony, especially considering the number of blue-skinned inhabitants living on its side of Malaz Island.
Jakatakan
Based on its usage,
Jakatakan
in most cases meant 'from Jakata'. However, Jakata or the area around it may, in fact, have been called Jakatakan in the past and it was sometimes still used (in that form) by natives of the city (e.g., by
Bottle
). In some cases, the phrase indicated an origin from, or the location of,
Malaz Island
as a whole.
The Island is named Jakatakan on the map of the
Lands of Fist
.
When asked where he was selling appeasement dolls when he was younger, Bottle answered, "Jakatakan".
Bottle remembered that once upon a time, there had been apes on 'Malaz Island'. He remembered seeing a cage of them "in Jakatakan" when he was about seven years old. He mentioned the dockside market in Jakatakan.
Uru Hela
had once stowed aboard a Jakatakan merchanter.
Banaschar talked about wine served at
Coop
's as having been made from Jakatakan grapes.
Religion
Banaschar
had once been a priest of
D'rek
in the Jakatakan temple on Malaz Island.
Fashion
Mosel
had his hair braided and cut finger-length in the fashion of Jakatakan pirates.
The Jakatan style was to carry curved short swords sheathed pommel-forward.
Military
The
Jakatakan Élites
, renowned for their superior discipline and training, were likely either based in Jakata or had their origins in the city.
Shipping
The
Malazan Empire
gave charters to Jakatan vessels allowing them to intercept non-Imperial shipping off the coast of
Quon Tali
thus permitting the cities long tradition of piracy to survive.
The Jakatakan fleet patrolled the seas from Malaz Island west, to the island of Geni and on to the Horn of the mainland. At full strength, it comprised twenty-seven dromons and sixteen resupply ships.
At the time that four Malazan dromons, carrying the flags of the Jakatakan fleet, entered Malaz City harbour, the fleet had lost a number of ships clashing with an unknown foe. It was rumoured that eleven ships had been lost but that number was unconfirmed. The four dromons had delivered castaways from a remote reef island southwest of the Horn.
When
Adjunct
Tavore
arrived at Malaz City, a longboat from the Jakatakan fleet's flagship drew up alongside her flagship, the
Froth Wolf
, to convey the Jakatakan Commander,
Exent Hadar
with a message for the Adjunct.
The
Bonehunters
gave the Jakatakan dromons a memorable send-off as the dromons slid past them. Those on the
Silanda
for example, held some of the animated
Tiste Andii
heads under their arms which left the unseasoned
Untan
soldiers aboard the Jakatakan vessels scared witless.
Notable characters from Jakata
Bottle
Inkaras Sollit
In
The Bonehunters
It was rumoured that the priests and priestesses of D'rek's temple in Jakata had vanished because the goddess hungered for
Wickan
blood and sent her clergy on the hunt for any who remained on Malaz Island.
In all likelihood, the temple faithful had met the same fate inflicting the other D'rek temples of the world.

======================================================================
PAGE: Jick
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Jick
======================================================================

Jick
was a fortress city considered to be the most secure of all the settlements in the
Falari Isles
.
It was built into the cliffs of the rugged
Walk Mountains
on the northwest shore of the
Walk Sea
and featured a narrow harbour filled with fishing vessels and merchant ships.
The town was governed by a ruling family and mayor.
The local temple of
Mael
was led by a ranking priest named
Gaddeth
.
In
Forge of the High Mage
Malazan
Emperor
Kellanved
devised an attack on the Falari Isles using a fleet of freebooters to spread out and terrorise the local settlements. A group of five pirate ships, including that of
Captain
Balethen
, conquered the city overnight by entering the city's harbour and setting all the other vessels alight. In the ensuing chaos, they secured the fortress' main tower and threw the city's ruling family to their deaths. The pirates held the city at their drunken mercy, meeting refusals and complaints from the citizens with the sword. After the mayor was likewise thrown to his death, Gaddeth became the unwilling representative of the people.
Gaddeth's spirits rose during his weekly magical communion with his fellow priests across the islands when he learned Kellanved had been killed by the
Cult of Mael
's
Jhistal
. Racing to the city keep to inform the invaders their leader was dead, he was astonished when the drunken Balethen and the others broke into celebration rather than flee for their lives.

PAGE: Jook
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Jook
======================================================================

Jook
was a city on the southern coast of
Jook Isle
near the
Jook Strait
in the
Falari Isles
. To its north were
Cutip
and
Curaca
, and to its east was
Gung
.
Notable residents
Jensk
, captain of the
Irene
In
Forge of the High Mage
After
Gianna
escaped from the
Cult of Mael
in
Cabil
, she made her way to Jook. There she was taken on as a veteran hand by
Captain
Jensk
to help his ancient, dilapidated merchant coaster, the
Irene
, in the crossing to
Belade
.
Malazan
Emperor
Kellanved
devised an attack on the Falari Isles using a fleet of freebooters to spread out and terrorise the local settlements, and the pirate captain,
Tereth
quickly seized Curaca.
Falar
's
Guiding Council of the Faith
attempted to coordinate an attack on Curaca to retake the island, but the most powerful Falari cities (
Delanss
and
Strike
) insisted on maintaining their own defences foremost.
The de facto ruler of the council,
Mallick Rel
, then proposed using the
Jhistal
to sweep clean the entirety of Jook Island, killing the invaders. The other council members were horrified at the idea of killing their own citizens and destroying their own cities, so Mallick agreed to hold off for two days so that the priests on the island could give word to whatever faithful remained to evacuate.
This ultimately failed go come to pass because the
Cult of Mael
lost command of the Jhistal.

Quon Tali
Kan
was the capital city of the

In
House of Chains
After promising to return

,

, and

Shadowthrone

Kanarbar Belid
was a long-extinct city in the north of the
Seven Cities
sub-continent. During the time of the
First Empire
, the
T'rolbarahl
,
Dejim Nebrahl
, had hunted there for blood. Only dust remained where the city once stood.
In
The Bonehunters
After being driven away from a slave caravan by
Iskaral Pust
, Dejim Nebrahl had been unable to find food in the plague-ridden region.  Fevered and starved, the T'rolbarahl journeyed to Kanarbar Belid and other old hunting grounds hoping to find human prey.  He found only dust and memories.
Trivia
The glossary of
The Bonehunters
describes Kanarbar Belid as the "old name for  Belid, city in Seven Cities" much the way
Inath'an Mersin
is defined as the old name for
Mersin
. While Mersin appears on maps of Seven Cities, Belid does not. It is unclear if the glossary is in error or if the Seven Cities map is incomplete.

======================================================================
PAGE: Kansu
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Kansu
======================================================================

Seven Cities
Kansu
was a squalid port city with six piers on the northwest extremity of the
Ehrlitan Sea
.
Within the city was a Temple of
D'rek
where the area's foremost healers could be found.
The inland road leading from the city was crowded with a sprawl of shanties before opening to herd lands and
Tharok
orchards.
The
Kansu Reach
ran eastward from the city along the
A'rath Strait
.
In
The Bonehunters
Nok
's fleet wrecked four of Kansu's piers as part of
Malazan
pacification efforts against the
Whirlwind
rebellion.  A modest
garrison
was established with the Malazan soldiers mostly guarding the gates and docks.
After his time at the
Finnest House
in
Darujhistan
,
Ganoes Paran
travelled by ship to Kansu.
Apsalar joined him in the A'rath Strait, only departing his company once they reached a crossroads outside Kansu.
Apsalar had noticed a strange mood and emptiness about the city, which Paran attributed to the arrival of
Poliel
's plague.  When city officials sought help from the healers of the D'rek temple, they found everyone within slaughtered.

PAGE: Karakarang
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Karakarang
======================================================================

Karakarang
was one of the
Holy Cities
of
Seven Cities
. It was located on
Otataral Island
in the northeast part of the continent.
Specifically, it lay on an outjut of land bordered by the
Talgai Sea
on the west, the
Bandiko Sea
to the north, and the
Sea of Gallada
to the east.
It was the Holy City of the
Tanno
cult.
Tanno
drakes
brought pilgrims to
Rutu Jelba
from where a pilgrim route led over the
Talgai Mountains
to Karakarang.
The nearby isles were likely the
Karang Isles
.
In
Deadhouse Gates
Fiddler
,
Kalam Mekhar
,
Crokus Younghand
and
Apsalar
took passage as crew on a
Blue Moranth
trader from
Genabackis
to the imperial port of Karakarang. They then travelled on the
Tano
pilgrim route from Karakarang across the
Talgai Mountains
down to Rutu Jelba.
Fiddler later pondered that the whores of Karakarang had looked like poxed sisters from some gigantic poxed family with poxed babies on their hips.
Turqa
, the captain of Kimloc's private guard, told Fiddler that he had been
Kimloc
's first guest in the eleven years since the
Spiritwalker
negotiated the peaceful surrender of Karakarang to the
Malazan Empire
with
High Fist
Dujek Onearm
. Turqa disclosed to
Fiddler
that although Kimloc could have destroyed the advancing Malazan forces, he chose to surrender in order to prevent the city from sharing the fate of
Aren
whose inhabitants had been slaughtered by the
T'lan Imass
. The time reference puts the surrender at around 1153
BS
.
In
Memories of Ice
Quick Ben
claimed that a sorceress going by the name of
Nightchill
had been involved when, nine centuries before the start of the
Malazan Book of the Fallen
, Karakarang was liberated from unknown occupiers.
Natives
Ebron

Seven Cities detail
Seven Cities
Karashimesh
(or
Karaschimesh
)
was one of
Seven Cities
' holy cities. It was an ancient city
located on the northern shore of the
Karas Sea
.
Kalam Mekhar
worked in Karashimesh during his pre-Imperial days with his partner
Porthal K'nastra
.
It was said that
Sergeant
Borduke
once threw a nobleborn officer off a cliff near Karashimesh.
Hyenas were sometimes spotted in the area, a rare sight east of
Aren
.
Notable residents
Torahaval Delat
In
The Bonehunters
Karashimesh was one of several ancient cities in the centre of the Seven Cities subcontinent that were home to a mostly subjugated people characterised by blonde hair, heart-shaped faces, and blue eyes.  It was implied they were the remnants of the original people of the
First Empire
as they shared these physical characteristics with the people of the
Kingdom of Lether
, a one-time First Empire colony.  Other cities whose populations included these remnant peoples were
Halaf
,
Guran
, and
Omari
.

======================================================================
PAGE: Kartool
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Kartool
======================================================================

Quon Tali
Kartool City
was located on
Kartool Island
, off the east coast of
Quon Tali
. It was known for its impressive population of deadly fist-sized
paralt
spiders whose webs festooned the city's score of towers.
Gulls and pigeons could often be spotted entangled in the paralt's webs and the arachnids' moult-skins and web-fragments polluted the city's murky harbour.
The city was bordered by a ring of limestone cliffs.
Citizens dressed as giant spiders during the Paralt Festival.
Conquered by the
Malazan Empire
decades ago, it was ruled by an Imperial
Fist
and an Imperial
garrison
was maintained within the city.
The city guard commander had an office in the Imperial Domicile.
The city was once the centre of worship for the island's patron goddess,
D'rek
, but the Empire had suppressed the cult and its practices.
During the Clear Season of autumn, prevailing winds made travel to
Malaz Island
and the south virtually impossible for two months.
Recruiting drives for the
Malazan Military
rarely garnered more than a handful of Kartoolians, and those were mostly destitute or criminals.
Notable locations
Free Docks
Grand Temple of D'rek
Imperial Domicile
Septarch District
Street of the Icon Carvers
History
Kartool by
Corporal Nobbs
Before the founding of the Malazan Empire, Kartool had been a target of the
Kingdom of Unta
.  Unta annexed the
Napan Isles
to serve as a staging point for an invasion of Kartool.
At a later date,
Admiral Nok
had sought to challenge Kartool's fleet of three pirate vessels, which had been blessed by priests of D'rek.  After a disastrous attempt to restock their water supplies on the Napan Isles, Nok's six ships were forced to return to
Nap
.  Nok returned the following year and crushed Kartool's tiny fleet.  Two months later the island was conquered.
A great battle had been fought by the Malazan Emperor
Kellanved
's
T'lan Imass
at Kartool.
Adjunct
Lorn
spoke of clan chieftain
Eitholos Ilm
standing alongside
Bonecaster
Olar Ethil
during an exchange of sorcery that made the battle between the Empire and
Moon's Spawn
at the
Siege of Pale
"look like a child's cantrip".
The timeline for the battle is unclear, however it is likely meant to have been the Malazan invasion which
Hellian
said took place decades earlier than 1164
BS
. The Emperor's main target on the island had been the cult of D'rek whose priests and priestesses were master sorcerors. They were ruled over by the
Demidrek
and were the heart of Kartool's power. The night before the great naval battle and the subsequent invasion, under
Dancer
and
Surly
's lead, the cult's sorcerors, including the Demidrek, had been thoroughly obliterated.
The Malazans immediately abolished slavery, closed the city's
Execution Pits
, and eliminated the
Istral'fennidahn
celebrations of D'rek.
The incumbent archpriest of the Grand Temple in the years 1164 BS had gained his eminence in an internal coup not so long ago, ousting his rival
Tayschrenn
who had been the Emperor's new (at the time)
High Mage
.
Temples
Kartool by
Shadaan
Once, only seven religions had been permitted upon Kartool Island. That of D'rek, which was the most influential, and six others subservient to her. Temples to D'rek,
Soliel
,
Poliel
,
Beru
,
Burn
,
Hood
and
Fener
were found in the
Septarch District
of the city of Kartool, hence the name. Since coming under the control of the Malazan Empire, the situation had changed and a modest Temple of the
Queen of Dreams
, a much-despised one of
Shadow
as well as temples to
Dessembrae
,
Togg
and
Oponn
had appeared.
The Grand Temple of D'rek was the largest structure in the city, but was left in a state of disrepair.
The other temples fared little better and the ornate architecture of the Septarch District's decrepit towers and domes was festooned with paralt webbing and chitinous rubbish.
In
The Bonehunters
Having been requested by the visiting priest
Banaschar
, a squad of the Septarch District city guard under
Sergeant
Hellian broke down the locked doors to the Grand Temple of D'rek and found the remnants of a massacre with all of the temple's residents slaughtered.
Notable Kartoolians
Allatch
Brethless
Burnt Rope
Commander
Charl
Feneresh
Sergeant
Hellian
Hunt
Imarish Laccon
Ithell
Koarsden Taneth
Noto Boil
Reuthen
Salleen
Shijel
Silla Leansath
Tayschrenn
Touchy
Corporal/Sergeant
Urb

Seven Cities
Kayhum
was a major city
located south of the
Thalas Mountains
on

.  The
River Ugarat
that passed the town continued southwards to
Ugarat
.  To the northwest of the city was
Y'Ghatan
.
Over a thousand years ago it had been one of a dozen great cities around the
Ugarat Odhan
linked to Ugarat by active caravan routes.  Only Kayhum's location on the banks of the river saved it from the region's desertification.  All of Ugarat's other satellite cities had long crumbled and turned to dust.

PAGE: Kharkanas
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Kharkanas
======================================================================

Central Kharkanas
For the Malazan prequel trilogy, see
Kharkanas Trilogy
.
Kharkanas
[kar-KAN-as],
the First City of Dark,
was the
Tiste Andii
capital of the
Hold of Darkness
,
also given the honourific 'Wise Kharkanas'.
It was bisected by the
Dorssan Ryl
river.
Only one of royal Tiste Andii blood could make a true claim to the throne.
The throne room in the palace was reached via stairs. There was a marble banister at the top of the stairs. The room itself had several entrances and was dominated by black stone and black wood. The floor had a crimson and onyx mosaic. The throne was raised on a knee-high dais that was the stump of a
blackwood
tree, roots of which snaked down into the surrounding floor. The throne itself had been carved from the bole, a simple, almost ascetic chair. One side entrance had a pedestal to either side on which stood black lacquered amphora, one of which broke when flung by
Sandalath Drukorlat
in a fit of temper.
The adjective "Kharkanan" was used to refer to something of or related to Kharkanas.
In the Andii game of
Kef Tanar
, the fifty or more tiles making up the Grand City during play represented Kharkanas.
In
Toll the Hounds
Endest Silann
recalled the Andii legends that said his people originated in forests and clearings and were given birth to give breath to the sacred wood. The first fall of his people occurred when they left the woods to set down the first stone of Kharkanas.
(Information needed)
In
Dust of Dreams
Queen of the
Shake
Yan Tovis
and her brother,
Yedan Derryg
titled "The Watch" led their people and a mass of
Letherii
refugees from the foundering prison of
Second Maiden Fort
to
Blind Gallan
's road. After travelling the path and encountering
Tiste Liosan
and
Forkrul Assail
, the exodus of ten thousand found the city of Kharkanas abandoned. But the refugees took shelter there and tried to return to normality while Yedan and Yan Tovis prepared to defend the city against invasion by the Tiste Liosan.
Mother Dark
returned to Kharkanas, something that would be sensed by all Tiste Andii.
In
The Crippled God
Sandalath Drukorlat was the first Andii to return to Kharkanas where, as the only Tiste Andii present, she reluctantly accepted the role as Queen of Kharkanas.
As the Liosan breached Lightfall and their legions attempted to sack Kharkanas and kill Mother Dark, Sandalath spiraled into madness remembering the horrors of the past that took place within the palace; the noble families often exchanged
Hostages
(Sand being among them) with many raised against a backdrop of constant backstabbing, murder, and finally with the fall of Kharkanas, bloody anarchy. Sand's husband
Withal
, who came to Kharkanas with her, was unable to stop her decline.
Yedan, Yan Tovis, the Shake, and Letherii were able to defend the
First Shore
long enough for
Nimander Golit
to lead the Andii home from
Black Coral
; after defeating the Liosan at the Shore, the Andii invaded the city of the Liosan to put an end to the endless war.
In
Forge of Darkness
Map of Kurald Galain
(Information needed)
In
Fall of Light
(Information needed)

Kolanse
Unofficial Malaz World Map by D'rek
Kolanse
was a region to the east of the continent of
Lether
, past the
Wastelands
and the
Glass Desert
.
Estobanse
Province, was the richest land of the Kolanse, thriving on springs. The southern kingdoms suffered from droughts, however.
Overfarming of thin topsoil led to spreading desertification that left Kolanse teetering on the edge of starvation.
Several decades before the start of the
Malazan Book of the Fallen
, Kolanse had experienced a series of cyclically expansionist regimes which drove the tribes of
Lether
's plains westward against the frontier of the
Letherii Empire
.
Following a civil war, Kolanse retreated into isolation.

infiltrated the

Korel,
aka
Lands of Fist
Lallit
was a port city on the western coast of
Rool
. It was a modest town with a narrow harbour opening onto the
Sender's Sea
.
The tower of the Sea-Gate overlooked the harbour.
In
Stonewielder
After the
Malazan Expeditionary Force
invaded Rool, Overlord
Yeull 'ul Taith
brought his troops to Lallit.  From there they embarked on a voyage down the
Crack Strait
to
Korelri
to ally with the
Stormguard
.
Commander
Borun
and his thousand
Black Moranth
were left behind and abandoned.  Ultimately a lone
Blue Moranth
vessel from the Expeditionary Force arrived in Lallit's harbour to reach terms with their cousins.

PAGE: Lamentable Moll
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Lamentable_Moll
======================================================================

Lamentable Moll
, or simply
Moll
, was a port city in
Theft
, governed by King
Seljure
. It was described as having "slate-covered barrows humped the streets, tilted the houses and cramped the alleyways in every quarter".
In at least some cases, homes were built directly on top of barrows so that their floors were buckled and misshaped by the humped structures underneath.
The city  was known for its minor sorcerers, diviners, readers, warlocks, and well-sounders.

In
Blood Follows
During the visit of infamous necromancers
Bauchelain
and
Korbal Broach
, the city was plagued by a series of shocking murders.  In this same period the pair took on
Emancipor Reese
as their manservant.
In
Upon a Dark of Evil Overlords
Emancipor Reese recalled how his childhood home had been built directly on top of one of Lamentable Moll's barrows, causing the floor to be humped. Once a ghost had waded through the room where Reese slept with only its head and chest above the floor. It had turned to look at the young boy and stuck its tongue out at him.
Trivia
Life in Lamentable Moll was quite different than on the rest of the
Korel
continent.  As depicted in
Stonewielder
, magic and religious worship were strictly controlled by the continent's patron goddess,
the Lady
.  Yet in
Blood Follows
,
mages
and worship of foreign gods appeared to be unrestricted. It is unclear whether this was due to some special property of the city or merely a continuity error between books.

Quon Tali
Larent
was a city on the southeastern coast of
Quon Tali
.  It was located where two great rivers that crossed the continent emptied into the
Bloor Sea
. To its south was
Yellows
and to its east was
Sentry
.  Upriver from Larent was the city of
Bloor
.
In
Kellanved's Reach
In the formative days of the
Malazan Empire
, the noble ruler of Larent raised a regiment to fight with the united forces of the
Bloorian League
against the forces of
Gris
and its allies.
In
Forge of the High Mage
In preparation for the Malazan invasion of
Falar
, Emperor
Kellanved
visited Larent and other ports aboard the
Twisted
with
Admiral
Cartheron Crust
seeking to recruit a fleet of "sea-borne thieves, petty smugglers, coastal raiders and slavers" to serve as the
navy's
vanguard. At Larent, they found many candidates.

Seven Cities detail
Lato Revae
was a small city
which lay on the western edge of
Raraku
and to the northeast of the
Thalas Mountains
in
Seven Cities
.  To its north lay the island city of
Longshan
.
A
Malazan
-built imperial road connected the city to
Ugarat
.
The lands southwest of the city towards the
Mersin River
were relatively crowded by Seven Cities' standards.  Irrigation ditches ribboned the plain, while wells, groves, roads, and villages were everywhere.
Notable residents
Untural
In
House of Chains
Karsa Orlong
skirted the city on his way from Raraku to the
Jhag Odhan
.
In
The Bonehunters
As the
14th Army
made its pursuit of the remnants of the
Army of the Whirlwind
, rumours spread among the 14th that a new contingent of recruits and officers had disembarked at Lato Revae and were struggling to catch up.

======================================================================
PAGE: Lest
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Lest
======================================================================

Map showing the spread of the Pannion Domin.
The city-state of
Lest
was far to the east of the Free City of
Darujhistan
and four days' march south of
Capustan
.
The walled city was known for its raised gardens.
Lest and the nearby city of
Setta
were producers of fine silks of pale yellow.
The citizens were referred to as Lestari.
A branch of the
D'Arle
noble merchant family lived in Lest. They were relatives of
Kalan D'Arle
of Capustan and
Estraysian
and
Challice D'Arle
of
Darujhistan
.
In
Memories of Ice
In the months leading to the
Siege of Capustan
, Lest was annexed by the
Pannion Domin
.
Like Setta and
Maurik
it was depopulated and emptied of life in the process. Only a few charred bones and the wreckage of burned buildings remained.
Survivors of the Lestari Palace Guard made their way to Capustan.
After defeating
Septarch
Kulpath
's forces at Capustan,
Caladan Brood
's army "liberated" Lest on its way to Maurik where it was to reunite with
High Fist
Dujek Onearm
's allied army.
In
Toll the Hounds
A year after the Pannion Domin's downfall, Lest remained a dead city.
Notes and references
Notes
Among the silks the man recognized the dyed lavender twists and bolts of
Illem
, the pale yellows of Setta and Lest - two cities to the southeast he knew had been annexed by the
Pannion Seer
in the last month - and the heavy bold twists of
Sarokalle
.
•
GotM, US HC, p.169

Map of Lether and Kolanse by
Joshua Butler
The
continent
of
Lether
[Leather
or LETH-er],
(not to be confused with the
Empire of Lether
) was the setting for the novels
Midnight Tides
,
Reaper's Gale
,
Dust of Dreams
, and
The Crippled God
. It lay on the other side of the globe from the
Malazan Empire
. The mapped portion of the continent seen in
Midnight Tides
extended for over 600 leagues from north to south and for nearly 700 leagues from east to west. The map in
Reaper's Gale
was significantly larger in scope, but did not have a scale.
To the west of Lether lay the
Domain Ocean
. To the northwest was the
Calash Sea
, in the south lay the inland
Dracons Sea
, and to the northeast, the
Bluerose Sea
.
Nations
Ak'ryn
Awl'dan
Bluerose
Bolkando Kingdom
D'aliban
Deal
Descent

Drene
D'rhasilhani
Edur confederation
Isthmus
Karn
Korshenn
Kryn
Lekester
Letherii Empire
Pilott
Saphinand Kingdom
T'roos
Truce
Flora and fauna
Ash moth

Capabara fish
Grishol

(or Jarack)

In
Midnight Tides
Detail of Edur Lands and the North Lether frontier
Many millennia before the start of the series, the
Tiste Andii
and
Tiste Edur
armies of
Silchas Ruin
and
Scabandari Bloodeye
made war on the
K'Chain Che'Malle
in northwestern Lether. In the aftermath,
Mael
asked
Gothos
to preserve the battleground in ice. Gothos conducts a ritual of
Omtose Phellack
that sealed the land and prevented the evolution of magic on the western part of the continent.
Whereas in other places these Holds would evolve into the more refined magic form of
warrens
, sorcery in western Lether remained based on Holds.
At the same time,
Hood
and his warren were unknown in the
Kingdom of Lether
and the surrounding lands.
Even knowledge of the
Hold of Death
became lost and the paths of the dead in Lether were obscured, making the region prone to loitering ghosts, shades, and the undead.
In
Reaper's Gale
Empire of Lether
Northwest Lether saw many climactic changes as a result of the dissolution of Gothos' ritual. A maelstrom of ice and bergs broke apart and moved south, devouring the coast of
the Reach
and filling the waters around
Second Maiden Fort
. Glaciers in the northern
Bluerose Mountains
began to rapidly shrink and move once more, threatening the destruction of
Andara
and releasing carcasses and artifacts kept trapped for millennia.
In
Dust of Dreams
(Information needed)

======================================================================
PAGE: Letheras
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Letheras

Central Letheras
Empire of Lether and its neighbours
Letheras
[leh-THAIR-as]
was the capital city of the
Kingdom of Lether
, the largest and richest city on the
Lether
continent,
and the site of the
Imperial Palace
. It was the most populous city in the Letherii Empire with over a hundred thousand residents.
It was a walled city of domes, terraces, garishly painted buildings, towers, and platforms--many obscured by a haze of smoke.
The
Lether River
passed through the city's centre and the city was crisscrossed by canals, magnificent bridges, and multi-leveled tiers.
The city was a crowded, sordid maze.
Many of its narrow, twisted, garbage strewn alleys never knew the light of day as they were crowded overhead with balconies, ledges, and projections that served as makeshift roofs.
The city's wealthy kept their fortunes hidden within walled estates while the streets swelled with lost and indigent
Indebted
and tribal refugees.
The huge, double main gate in the city's white walls led to a cobblestoned imperial road wide enough to fit ten columns of soldiers.
Along the wall were sunken posterns, whose tunnels invited breaching, but which could be flooded at the pull of a lever. Each ended in a thick wooden door.
Two thousand paces beyond the city's western wall was
Kravos Hill
.
There were also several shanty-towns outside the city wall.
During the heat of the summer months, shops stayed open late into the night and the streets were crowded with shoppers.
Economy
Letheras by
Shadaan
The
Merchant Tolls
, a kind of stock market, listed Letheras' gross value at between twelve and fifteen
Peaks
with possibly another five buried.
In recent years, the eccentric
Tehol Beddict
had nearly caused the economy to crash through an unprecedented series of canny investments. In the end, Tehol's fortune crashed bringing down the fortunes of countless investors and causing the Tolls to write off an entire Peak as a loss. Ten thousand coins cursed against Tehol's name lay at the bottom of the city's canals.
Powerful guilds controlled the various industries within the city. They designated which companies could accept certain contracts, what wages and benefits could be paid, and kept blacklists of employees not eligible for guild jobs. Workers known as the Unwelcomes were often de-certified and removed from the guilds' working rolls for political reasons. The guilds were powerless to stop the Unwelcoms from being hired for jobs paying below the guilds' rates.
Some employers, such as the Royal Engineers, were required to hire only guild members.
The Chamber of Contracts and Royal Charters was responsible for assigning government work to the various guilds and assessing their progress.
Crime and Punishment
Order was maintained by the city garrison which had stations throughout the city.  In case of emergency, the stations used bells to summon other city guard units to their aid.
Squads of armed guards patrolled the city at night by lantern light. Near the Eternal Domicile, soldiers stood watch from corner blockhouses or at postern gates. Street intersections were lit by lantern poles.
See also:
The Drownings
Criminals who could not pay the fines to expunge their records were sentenced to swim the
Quillas Canal
while weighted down with coin. Few survived, and large crowds observed and placed wagers on the outcome.
Festivals
One of the holiday festivals celebrated by the people of Letheras was dedicated to the
Errant
. The festival was accompanied by frenzied wagering at the Special Drownings, which were reserved for the most notorious criminals. According to
Tehol Beddict
, the city's wealthy class used the festival to make public displays of their indolence.

History
The land where Letheras was founded was once a marshland basin fed by eleven rivers. Beneath the basin's brittle and porous crust was a vast underground chasm. Erosion eventually caused the basin to collapse resulting in a catastrophic draining of the area's rivers and swamps. All that remained of this cataclysm was
Settle Lake
, which despite its modest size was deceptively deep.
The city was settled by colonists of the
First Empire
many thousands of years before the current day and before that empire's downfall.
Most Letherii inaccurately believed the city was the site of the colonists' First Landing.
Letheras' first Royal Engineer,
Keden Qan
, conducted a thorough survey of the area at the time of its planning.
The
Old Palace
was built around a complex of three
Jaghut
towers and an
Azath Tower
so old as to predate the founding of the First Empire.
Qan's study showed that the Jaghut towers were part of a single and far larger complex, suggesting they were constructed prior to that race's dispersion.
A six-hundred-year-old proclamation forbid any attempt to demolish or resettle the area.
The Jaghut ruins and Azath Tower themselves appeared to be constructed on the ruins of a far older non-human settlement. Within most of the area covered by the modern city were ancient foundation walls, plazas and concourses, shaped wells, drainage ditches, and cemeteries. These formed a self-contained complex of intricately paved floors and streets entirely contained within multi-level roofing, with a second more defensible city below it. The underground corridors and tunnels were reused for the modern city's sewer system.
Virtually no artifacts were left behind by this mystery civilization, but there remained evidence that the residents made frantic attempts to insulate their dwellings. Qan theorised this was in response to catastrophic climate change.
Ancient tombs of origin unknown to the Letherii could still be found beneath the city, though most had collapsed or sunk into the mud. Their doors were covered with hieroglyphics which scholars had only partially deciphered to reveal as curse-laden and aspected to the
Errant
in some mysterious way. Few Letherii ever broke into the tombs as they were always empty and trespassers were reputed to die in horrific ways.
Bugg
claimed the tombs had been built and warded by the
Forkrul Assail
for the Jaghut in an attempt to provide haven from their enemies, the
T'lan Imass
.
Icarium
visited the city in ancient times and constructed a mysterious device beneath it.
In
Midnight Tides
Letheras by
Corporal Nobbs
The kingdom was at the height of its power and preparing for the
Seventh Closure
, the prophesied renaissance when the First Empire would be reborn and King Ezgara would
Ascend
and assume the title of First Emperor.
After seventeen years,
the
Eternal Domicile
was nearing completion to serve as the site of Ezgara's coronation.
It was revealed that Tehol Beddict's spectacular failure in the Tolls was in fact an ingenious ruse. With no one in the city the wiser, he had accumulated and disappeared a fortune from notice which he used to resettle the city's tribal refugees on newly purchased islands. The tribal mixed-bloods,
Shand
,
Rissarh
, and
Hejun
were the only ones to unravel his con. They convinced him to secretly repeat his plan but at a much higher level with the goal of crashing the Letherii economy to trigger a cultural reformation.
A disastrous war provoked by Queen
Janall Diskanar
, Prince
Quillas Diskanar
, and Chancellor
Triban Gnol
brought the
Tiste Edur
army of Emperor
Rhulad Sengar
to the city's doorstep. On the day of the Seventh Closure, Emperor Rhulad seized the city from the king and named himself emperor of the new Letherii Empire on the day of the Seventh Closure.
By the time it became clear that the Edur might win the war, Tehol had called a halt to his scheme. Although he was able to evacuate the city's refugee population before the city's occupation, he was not ready to trade the Letherii's corrupt civilization for the Edur's stagnant one.
In
Reaper's Gale
As the capital settled in under the rule of their Tiste Edur conquerors, two new organizations appeared in the city. The
Patriotists
under Invigilator
Karos Invictad
were officially chartered as the empire's secret police, launching a brutal reign of terror to root out traitors both real and imagined. Hundreds of citizens were arrested every week and many found their way to the Drownings, which were taken over by the Patriotists as a means of execution. At the same time, the capital's wealthiest families formed a loose consortium of businesses known as the
Liberty Consign of Merchants
and led by
Rautos Hivanar
.
Tehol Beddict and Bugg developed a new scheme to bring down the empire by acquiring and removing large quantities of imperial coin from circulation.
At the same time, Karos Invictad was conducting a similar scheme to strip the coffers of the Liberty Consign bare.
When the economy reached a crisis, angry mobs rioted in the city and the poorer districts in the north burned.
A mob lay siege to the compound of the Patriotists, setting it on fire, calling for the imprisoned Tehol's death, and killing a dozen agents.
Icarium
activated a millennia-old machine he had constructed on the site of the
Rat Catchers' Guild
. When he entered the device, it caused buildings all over the city to collapse and annihilated the entire neighbourhood around the Guild in white fire.
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
's
Bonehunters
invaded Lether in response to the Tiste Edur
fleet's
attack on
Sepik
.
The
Imperial Brigade
faced
Fist
Keneb
's
Marines
without conclusive result on Kravos Hill outside the city before being defeated by the Adjunct's main force near the Lether River. The Malazan marines found a hidden entrance beneath the city walls and seized the city's western gate to allow the rest of the army entrance. Four squads of marines simultaneously conducted guerrilla warfare within the city to keep the City Garrison busy.
Fiddler
,
Quick Ben
, and
Hedge
delivered
Silchas Ruin
a decisive rebuke as the
Soletaken
Eleint
attempted to take vengeance on the city and its patron, the
Crippled God
. Then Fiddler's squad assaulted the Eternal Domicile where they slew Chancellor Triban Gnol. Once the main force of Malazans entered the city, the City Garrison surrendered and the city fell.
The Tiste Edur abandoned the city, returning to their homeland in the north. Some had departed at Hannan Mosag's behest, while the others left with
Hanradi Khalag
after their betrayal by the Letherii at Kravos Hill.
Rhulad Sengar was slain in his arena by
Karsa Orlong
ending the immortal Edur emperor's reign.
Rucket
and
Ormly
spent a fortune hiring criers to proclaim Tehol a hero of the people who eliminated everyone's debt to successfully turn public sentiment back in his favour. When Adjunct Tavore and the marines reached the Eternal Domicile, Rucket introduced
Brys Beddict
as Lether's saviour and Tehol as Lether's new emperor.
Janath Anar
married Tehol becoming both his empress and the empire's new chancellor.
In
Fall of Light
Letheras may have been built on the site of the ancient Jaghut capital of
Omtose Phellack
. The
Seregahl
who were released from the dying Azath Tower in Letheras in
Midnight Tides
, were imprisoned there when
Hood
challenged them to prove their worth as the vanguard of the army which was assembling to march on Death itself. In exchange, the Azath House released
Gethol
, brother of
Gothos
.
Trivia
According to author
Steven Erikson
, some of the inspiration for Letheras came from the city of
Venice
, which is famous for its canals and its steady subsidence into the lagoon it is built upon. And "at the height of their power, they were all about wealth, and...looting everything they could in the
Mediterranean
and beyond." Erikson thought it was "a great metaphor for capitalism itself...you have to keep building on top of it because the foundations keep sinking into the mud."

======================================================================
PAGE: Li Heng
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Li_Heng
======================================================================

Li Heng
Quon Tali
Interpretation of Li Heng in Return of the Crimson Guard by
Shadaan
"
Strong as the walls of Heng
"
―Common saying in Quon Tali
Li Heng
was an inland
Quon Talian
city situated just north of the
Dal Hon Plains
on the
Idryn
river. It straddled the famed
Trunk Road
trade route connecting
Unta
in the east to
Quon Tali
in the west making trade its lifeblood.
The city was famous for its titanic walls which could be seen from as far as a day's travel away.
The walls divided the city into concentric rings known as Rounds. Each Round was walled, with the height of each crenelated wall growing as one moved closer to the centre of the city. From a distance this made the city resemble a "layered plateau."
The outermost wall was "ten man-heights high"
The innermost Round was known as the Inner Focus and contained the
Palace / City Temple
complex at the centre. Moving outwards, the next Round was the Greater Immediate Round, which housed the city's aristocracy, government officials, and wealthy merchants, followed by the Lesser Immediate Round, which was the city's centre of commerce. The final Outer Round was filled with crowded tenements, factories, corrals, and ghettoes.
There were four main gates in the city's outer wall, the
Gate of the Dawn
to the East, the
Gate of the Dusk
to the West, the
Gate of the Mountains
to the South, and the
Gate of the Plains
to the north.
Locals believed the outer wall had once been ringed by a moat, but test digs by Malazan engineers revealed only the presence of a ditch littered with rubbish and animal carcasses.
Gates between Rounds were staggered for defensive purposes, preventing invaders from taking a single straight passage to the heart of the city.  The increasing heights of each wall provided safety to the inner Rounds if the outer Round ever fell. The Idryn river's path through the centre of the city was straddled by several thick portcullis-bearing River Gates blocking water traffic from passing between the city's Rounds.
In the entirety of the city's existence, its walls had never been breached by invaders. Even its Malazan conquerors had been forced to use non-traditional means.
The area surrounding the city was cultivated for grain and spotted with market gardens, and peasants raised sheep, hogs, and cattle.
Animal manure was used as fuel for heating and cooking as the plains were largely barren of trees.
Under Malazan administration the city was governed by a
Ruling Council of Magistrates
.
The
City Temple
had been re-sanctified to the Malazan gods, heroes, and guardians spirits.
The terms "Hengan" (plural form "Hengans") or "Hengese" were used to describe people or objects related to the city.
Hengans elongated their vowels in speech.
Heavy mouths were a physical characteristic typical of Hengans.
The city's patron deity was
Burn
.
Not far east of the city was the
Great Sanctuary of Burn
, the continent's largest monastery until it was eventually destroyed by an earthquake.
In areas of the city, a raised boardwalk fronted by inns and bars ran along the Idryn waterfront. During dry summers, the river lowered exposing the boardwalk's pilings and revealing expanses of thick mud and sewer filth.
History
Li Heng was one of several major city-states to rise on Quon Tali, and was once the third most powerful such state on the continent.
Sometime before the rise of the Malazan Empire, but still within living memory, it had formed the despotic Li Heng League.
In addition to contesting with the region's other major city-states, Li Heng was also at constant war with the
Seti
and their man-jackal god,
Ryllandaras
. The city's great walls were built to keep them out.
Those peasants outside the walls were forced to seek shelter in bolt-holes made of fieldstone scattered amongst the farm fields.
The city fell to outsiders for the first time about a century before the events depicted in the
Malazan Book of the Fallen
. During the reign of Li Heng's legendary Protectress
Shalmanat
, Malazan Emperor
Kellanved
brought his undead warriors, the
T'lan Imass
, and
Dancer
assassinated the Protectress in her throne room.
During this time it was also mandatory for mages to announce themselves upon entering the city. Of course many ignored this rule and found other ways within its walls.
Unlike most cities conquered by the Malazans it was not needed to outlaw any existing assassins guilds as there were none in operation at the time, rather individuals who might hire their services to criminal organizations.

In
Reaper's Gale
Throatslitter
's father told stories of the city's fall to the Malazans. On a spring morning after Kellanved had usurped the pirate
Mock
and taken control of
Malaz Island
, strange figures wearing furs and bone helmets and wielding misshapen swords and axes appeared suddenly on the battlements of the Palace of the Protectress. The palaces' vaunted Guard were not seen to challenge Kellanved's T'lan Imass even as tendrils of smoke rose from their barracks. Rumours held that the Protectress was seen falling from the High Tower by the City Temple. Thousands of T'lan Imass then emerged from the Inner Focus Gate to occupy the city. After a half-dozen suicidal skirmishes, the city's army surrendered and by day's end officers and nobles of the high court knelt in fealty before the future emperor.

Seven Cities
Lothal
was a city on the northern coast of the
Seven Cities
sub-continent. It was a port on the
Kokakal Sea
, northwest of the city of
Y'Ghatan
.  The city was ruled by a
Holy Falah'd
.
In
The Bonehunters
Leoman of the Flails
ordered the forced evacuation of Y'Ghatan's entire population to Lothal, prior to the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
.  He sent messengers to advise the city's Holy Falah'd to send his troops to manage the refugees along the road between the two cities, something the Falah'd was happy to do as it meant Leoman had no plans to visit Lothal.
Admiral
Nok
planned to land five thousand Malazan
Marines
at Lothal to aide
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
's investment of Y'Ghatan,
but the city was overtaken by the extremely virulent
plague
which was then sweeping across Seven Cities.

======================================================================
PAGE: Malaz City
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Malaz_City

Malaz City ca.1150 Burn's Sleep
Malaz Isle
Quon Tali
Malaz City by
Shadaan
Malaz City by
Corporal Nobbs
Malaz City
was an island city and the home of
Kellanved
,
the birthplace of his
Malazan Empire
. The city was located on the small
Malaz Island
which was found southeast of
Quon Tali
.  It was split into northern and southern halves by the confluence of the
North
and
South Malaz Rivers
which flowed from the
Firstsight Mountains
into
Malaz Bay
.
Along the northern edge of the city ran the 500 foot tall
Mock's Cliff
, upon which sat
Mock's Hold
, former pirate stronghold and now Imperial
Garrison
. The fortress was reached by a switchback of wide stone steps known as
Rampart Way
leading from the city below.
To the south the city was bounded by the
Ridger Wall
which ran in parallel to the
Ridger
hill.
Front Street in the harbour district was largely ancient warehouses interspersed with ramshackle taverns, inns, and tenement houses, all facing the piers. From there, a maze of dark and twisting narrow streets and alleys led further into the city. The city's larger estates butted up against the cliff wall below
Mock's Hold
. Also below the fortress was the Imperial Pier.
Ships docking in the harbour were subject to inspection by the city's Harbourmaster. The waters surrounding the piers were notorious for sharks and small leech-like eels.
According to
Felisin Paran
, the temple to
Fener
was located in (on the) Dockfront.
There was also a temple to
D'rek
in the city.
Several blocks from the harbour was the
Deadhouse
, a seemingly abandoned stone structure amidst an overgrown yard, which was studiously avoided by the local residents.
Outside the city, the
Jakata
road was lined with slums.
As the Empire increased in size, Malaz City lost all tactical and strategic value and began a downward slide into irrelevance.  Many of the city's influential residents relocated to the Imperial capital at
Unta
leaving many of the city's homes deserted.  Trade declined, warehouses decayed, and piers eroded.  Its primary value was as a military transit point.
With only one short cold season, the city tended to get hot and stinking.

Population
Original map of Malaz City environs by Steven Erikson (may no longer be canonical)
The city's residents were a mixed breed of human races as was common on the island.
Religions
Chem
, an ancient sea deity, was the object of an old sea cult in Malaz City.
Before the existence of the
Malazan Empire
, Malaz City regularly celebrated a number of festivals devoted solely to Chem.
City Watch
Law and order was maintained by the City Watch, which had a barracks near the Centre Docks
and a heavily fortified armoury at the base of
Rampart Way
.
The Watch was armed with pikes and used alarms to signal each other.
Animals
The city was known for a breed of dog called the
Malazan ratter
, which was bred for its fearless insanity.
In
Gardens of the Moon
In the 1154th year of Burn's Sleep
Surly
, the Imperial Regent,
leader of the
Claw
, and soon to be Empress, created laws prohibiting the use of unsanctioned sorcery in Malaz City.
Elements of the
3rd Army
rendezvoused with recruits and were sent to enforce the Imperial Regent's edict. The riots that followed engulfed a quarter of the town in flames.
The mage cadre that was sent in, all new and untested, lost control.
Whiskeyjack
sent
Dujek
and some sappers to control the fires.
In
Deadhouse Gates
The Claw assassin
Pearl
maneuvered
Kalam Mekhar
to the city aboard the
Ragstopper
for a confrontation with Empress Laseen.  Not intending to make it easy, Pearl stabbed Kalam in the side and tossed him overboard.  The
Bridgeburner
made his way to shore were he was pursued by multiple Hands of the Claw.
Kalam ultimately made his way to Mock's Hold where he and the Empress settled their differences.
That same night,
Fiddler
,
Apsalar
,
Crokus
, and
Rellock
passed through the
Azath
warren from
Seven Cities
and exited through the
Deadhouse
.
In
The Bonehunters
Interpretation of plaza in Malaz City by
slaine69
Interpretation of plaza at night in Malaz City by
slaine69
Banaschar
returned to Malaz City and frequented
Coop
's
Hanged Man Inn
after learning the fate of
D'rek
's priesthood around the world. He drank regularly with
Braven Tooth
,
Temper
, and
Foreigner
. His goal was to speak to High Mage
Tayschrenn
, who was holed up in Mock's Hold, but so far had been unsuccessful.
Empress Laseen and her retinue of
Untan
Imperial Guards and as many as six hundred Claws travelled to Malaz City aboard four ships to await the return of the fleet carrying
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
and the
14th Army
back from Seven Cities.
Mallick Rel
and
Korbolo Dom
were both imprisoned in Mock's Hold,
but the
Jhistal
priest used his time to undermine the Imperial power structure and secure his own rise to power. He convinced an unknown number of Laseen's Claws to secretly changed loyalties to himself as the Jhistal Master of his
Black Glove
cult.
He also isolated Tayschrenn's outside communication.
Korbolo Dom was elevated to High Fist while Mallick became one of Laseen's advisors.
By the time the Adjunct's fleet arrived in the harbour, the citizens of Malaz City had been inflamed by rumour and
Mockra
magic to seek the slaughter of the "treacherous"
Wickans
and
Khundryl
among the Adjunct's troops.
Mallick had made certain the City Watch was undermanned and its officers carefully selected for incompetence.
At the same, his agents used well-timed shouts and exhortations to make the crowd gathering to confront the Adjunct's ships at the waterfront even more angry and belligerent.
Tavore kept her fleet anchored in the harbour, only allowing the
Froth Wolf
and the
Silanda
to moor at the city pier.
While she travelled to Mock's Hold to meet with the Empress, the squads of
Balm
, Fiddler, and
Gesler
guarded the two ships. The mob soon engaged the
Marines
in a desperate battle to destroy their ships.
Meanwhile, several members of the 14th Army entered the city on their own business.
Fiddler sought out the armourer,
Tak
, to purchase more
munitions
-tossing
crossbows
.
Then he, Gesler, and
Stormy
met their old
Master Sergeant
, Braven Tooth, to drink and remember fallen friends.
Bottle
entered the city to retrieve Foreigner at the Adjunct's request.
Agayla
advised him the find the man at Coop's.
Hellian
fell overboard in the harbour and climbed onto the docks in search of a drink.
She stumbled upon the Black Glove's attempt to assassinate Banaschar, dispatching
Saygen Maral
and arresting the priest of D'rek before dragging him to
Smiley's
.
Tavore refused Laseen and Mallick's efforts to deliver up the Wickans and Khundryl as scapegoats.
She fled back to her ships, alongside Kalam Mekhar and
T'amber
, pursued by hundreds of Pearl's Claws. Their running battles took them all across Malaz City before Tavore alone safely reached the
Froth Wolf
.
Pearl managed to fatally poison Kalam before
Apsalar
returned the favour.
Shadowthrone brought the dying Kalam to an uncertain fate at the Deadhouse.
Before dawn, at least a thousand Malazans lay dead on the docks and Tavore's now renegade fleet left Malaz City.  But before they could clear the harbour,
Cartharon Crust
's vessel, the
Drowned Rat
, pulled alongside her flagship to deliver
Withal
,
Sandalath Drukorlat
,
Nimander Golit
,
Phaed
, Bottle,
Grub
, and
Lostara Yil
, among others.
In
Night of Knives
Later in 1154, after the Mouse Quarter riots and on the night of the
Shadow Moon
, the fortress of Mock's Hold was the site of Emperor
Kellanved
and
Dancer
's apparent assassination.
The streets also saw battles involving the
Shadow cult
, the
Hounds of Shadow
, and a renegade band of Bridgeburners.
In
Deadhouse Landing
Malaz City (Pre-Empire)
(Information needed)
In
Kellanved's Reach
(Information needed)
Trivia
A hand-drawn map of the city by authors
Steven Erikson
and
Ian C. Esslemont
was included in the PS Publishing edition of
Night of Knives
.
Esslemont describes the city as "an amalgam of various seedy ports and rundown waterfront dive towns that we'd been to", and both authors say Malaz City was somewhat inspired by
Belize City
of the early 1980s.

======================================================================
PAGE: Malazan world
CATEGORIES: Continents
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Malazan_world
======================================================================

World map by
Corporal Nobbs,
based on the version of D'rek
The
Malazan world
has no official unified name, although
Steven Erikson
has jokingly called it
"Wu"
.
The name has gained some traction amongst fans as an affectionate and informal term for the planet.
The Malazan world is a globe
and appears to be at least similar in size to Earth, and may be notably larger. No unified map of the entire planet has been published to date, although fans have frequently attempted to create one. According to Erikson, a world map may appear in the planned
Encyclopaedia Malazica
. He has also confirmed that rough sketches of such maps have already been created.
Broken Binding world map, 2025
In an interview with a Spanish fantasy blog, Erikson stated that the hand-drawn version of the Malazan world which he had at home was too large to be photocopied, however, that the maps created by fans were coming close. Alongside the interview the page displayed a version of D'rek's map. It is unclear if that choice was Erikson's or that of the website.
The Malazan planet has at least four moons, although only one is easily visible from the surface and known to the general population. Three other moons are perpetually occluded from the sun's light. Early historical texts suggested they were not always so difficult to see.
Constellations visible from the world included the
Roads of the Abyss
and the
Dagger
.
Geographic layout
Malazan World Map by
Werthead
There are at least six continents on the Malazan world according to
Midnight Tides
.
However,
Return of the Crimson Guard
suggests twelve major landmasses exist.
The definition of what constitutes a "continent", "subcontinent" or large island in the world has never been firmly defined.
The largest continent on the Malazan world has no overall name. This landmass's eastern region (comprising roughly one-third of the entire landmass) is known as
Seven Cities
. This region is separated from the rest of the landmass by the vast
Jhag Odhan
. To the west of this lies the kingdoms of
Nemil
and
Perish
, whilst to the south-west lies the substantial
Shal-Morzinn Empire
.
South of Seven Cities lies the
Falari Isles
and the small continent of
Quon Tali
. Quon Tali is the heartland of the
Malazan Empire
, which was born on
an island
just off its southern coast. The island of
Drift Avalii
is located some distance off its south-western coast.
The narrow
Strait of Storms
divides Malaz Island from the continent of
Korelri
. Korelri is a large landmass comprising two subcontinents,
Fist
and
Stratem
. Fist consists of a vast number of islands and a part of the adjacent landmass. The
Aurgatt Range
divides the lands of Fist from Stratem.
Stratem consists of several peninsulas, divided from one another by a large inlet known as the
Sea of Chimes
.
South-west of Korelri and Quon Tali, beyond a vast field of floating ice, lies the small island-continent of
Jacuruku
. Jacuruku is a land of harsh extremes, with burning deserts on the western side and verdant jungle on the eastern.
East of Seven Cities and north-east of Quon Tali, across
Seeker's Deep
, lies the continent of
Genabackis
. Genabackis is a narrow but long continent stretching for many hundreds of leagues from north to south. To the east of Genabackis lies the
Genostel Archipelago
, comprising one large island (itself large enough to be counted as a subcontinent) and many smaller ones. Further east still is the
Cabal Archipelago
, which may lie closer to the far western coast of Seven Cities.
Due east of Quon Tali and south-east of Genabackis lies the continent of
Assail
. This is a long, narrow landmass comprising of two distinct regions, Assail proper (which is regarded as a land of unrelenting hostility) and a more civilized peninsula area in the south, known as
Bael
.
East of Assail, south of western Seven Cities and south-west of Jacuruku, deep in the southern hemisphere, lies the large continent of
Lether
, named for its largest nation. Isolated from the rest of the world by distance and the immense ice fields near Jacuruku, Lether had little contact with other lands and nations prior to the arrival of the renegade Malazan
14th Army.
Landmasses
Seven Cities
- The largest continent in the world. Technically, this name refers only to the easternmost third of the landmass, which forms a distinct subcontinent. However, the name is commonly used to refer to the entire landmass.
Quon Tali
- Continent south of Seven Cities.
Falar
- A subcontinent branching from northern Quon Tali, also includes the Falari Isles.
Genabackis
- Continent east of Seven Cities.
Genostel
- A large island, possibly a subcontinent of Genabackis.
Fist-Stratem - Continent south of Quon Tali. Sometimes confusingly referred to as
Korel
.
Lands of Fist
- The subcontinent comprising the northern half of this continent, consisting of several islands.
Stratem
- The subcontinent comprising the southern half of this landmass.
Jacuruku
- Continent south-west of Fist-Stratem.
Assail
- Continent south-east of Genabackis.
Bael
- Subcontinent comprising the southern part of Assail.
Lether
- Continent east of Assail, south of Seven Cities and west of Jacuruku.
Sea of Glass
- A largely undescribed region far to the south of Stratem
Bodies of water
Seeker's Deep
, known as the
Meningalle Ocean
in Genabackis. Divides Seven Cities from Genabackis, with Quon Tali to the south-west.
The
Falari Sea
, the sea to the east of the Falari Isles and north-east of Quon Tali.
The
Walk Sea
, an internal waterway of the Falari Isles.
The

, an internal waterway of the Falari Isles.
The

The

, an inlet of the Seeker's Deep dividing
Otataral Island
from the
Hissar
region of Seven Cities.
The

, an inlet of the Seeker's Deep into eastern Seven Cities.
The

, an inlet of the Seeker's Deep into north-western Genabackis.
The
Owndos Sea
, an inland sea in Genabackis linked to the Malyn Sea by rivers.
The
Clatar Sea
, a large inland sea in Seven Cities.
The
Sea of Storms
, also called the Ocean of Storms. The sea dividing Quon Tali from both Jacuruku (to the south-west) and Korelri (to the south and south-east).
The
Cawn Sea
, an inlet of the Sea of Storms on the southern coast of Quon Tali.
The
Strait of Storms
, the straits dividing Malaz Island from Korelri.
The

The
Blackwater Strait
, one of the internal waterways of Fist.
The
Bloodmare Ocean
, the ocean lying to the east of Korelri.
The
Ice Island Sea
, the south-western part of the Bloodmare Ocean.
The
Horn Ocean
, the ocean lying to the south-west of Quon Tali and possibly along the south coast of Seven Cities.
The
Reacher's Ocean
, also called
The Reach
,
the ocean lying east of Quon Tali, north of Korelri, south of Genabackis and west of Assail.

Kartool
from the eastern coast of Quon Tali.

Rivan Sea
, the northern part of the Reacher's Ocean, lying along the south coast of Genabackis.
The
Galatan Sweep
, the sea to the east of the Rivan Sea, surrounding the 'fluke islands' of Genabackis.

Rust Ocean
, the ocean lying to the east of Genabackis.

Hudd Sea
, the sea lying along the north coast of Genabackis.

, the ocean lying to the north of Seven Cities.
The

, divides the island of
Sepik
from the north coast of Seven Cities.
The

, an inlet of the Dryjna Ocean into northern Seven Cities.
The
Maadil Sea
, an inlet of the Dryjna Ocean into northern Seven Cities.
The
Sea of Kaltepe Kadesh
, the sea lying to the north-east of Otataral Island.
The
Otataral Sea
, divides Otataral Island from north-eastern Seven Cities.
The
Bandiko Sea
, the sea lying to the north of Otataral Island.
The
Domain Ocean
, the ocean lying to the west of Lether and east of Assail.
The
Calash Sea
, the part of the Domain Ocean lying immediately north-west of the
Tiste Edur
tribal lands in northern Lether.
The
Dracons Sea
, an inlet of the Domain Ocean divided northern Lether from the peninsula lands to the south.
Sea Iban
, an inlet of the Domain Ocean on the far south coast of Lether.
The
Pelasiar Sea
, a large bay or sea in south-eastern Lether, south of
Kolanse
.
The
Bluerose Sea
, a semi-landlocked sea lying along the northern coast of Lether. It opens up into the wider ocean to the north.
The
White Spires Ocean
, an iceberg-blighted sea lying south of Jacuruku, south-west of Stratem and east of Lether.
The
Sea of Chimes
, an inlet of the White Spires Ocean in western Stratem.

Malazan globe model
There have been several efforts to display the Malazan world map on a globe. The first was created by Adam Whitehead and can seen
here.
Another globe model of the Malazan world was created by
Joshua Butler
at this
link.
Trivia
Steven Erikson
says the individual continental maps were created before their organized placement on the globe was decided. And since he and
Ian C. Esslemont
were always adding ice fields to the continental maps, it resulted in ice where it logically did not belong, such as on the equator. This led the two authors to create a reason for the ice's existence, leading to the background of the
Jaghut
and the
T'lan Imass
.

======================================================================
PAGE: Malyntaeas
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Malyntaeas
======================================================================

Northwest Genabackis
The city of
Malyntaeas
was situated on the western shore of the
Malyn Sea
in northwest
Genabackis
. The journey to Malyntaeas from
Tanys
took four days and three nights across the Malyn Sea.
Malyntaeas was founded by three very different tribes: the
Nathii
,
Genabarii
, and
Korhivi
and so was said to have the appearance of having been three separate cities at one time.
"
Three enormous stone fortifications commanded three distinct rises in the land, the centre one set back further from the shoreline than the other two.  Each possessed its own peculiar style of architecture.  The keep to the left was squat, robust and unimaginative, built of a golden, almost orange limestone that looked marred and stained in the sunlight. The centre fortification, hazy through the woodsmoke rising from the maze of streets and houses filling the lower tiers between the hills, appeared older, more decrepit, and had been painted - walls, domes and towers - in a faded red wash. The fortification on the right was built on the very edge of the coastal cliff, the sea below roiling amidst tumbled rocks and boulders, the cliff itself rotted, pock-marked and battle-scarred.
"
―Description of Malyntaeas from Chapter 2, HoC
The sloped walls of the third keep had deep cracks radiating out from the damaged sections and one of its square towers was leaning dangerously outward. A row of pennants could be seen beyond the wall. Every available space on the slopes and flat land around each of the three keeps was crowded by buildings, in style similar to their respective keep. The borders between the three different parts of the city were marked by wide street which wound inland.
The golden keep had once belonged to the Nathii, the red keep to the Genabarii, and the ruined keep to the Korhivi.
Only the presence of the
Malazan
Fist
serving as overlord and three companies from the
Ashok Regiment
kept the three racial factions from each other's throats.
The port possessed at least one broad stone pier and the city's bay was crowded with the boats of fishermen and traders.
In
House of Chains
Karsa Orlong
and
Torvald Nom
were transferred by ship from Tanys to Malyntaeas where they picked up six squads of the 2nd Company (Ashok Regiment). From Malyntaeas they continued onwards towards
Genabaris
.
The
Crimson Guard
were said to be in the city stirring up the Korhivi at around the time of Karsa and Torvald's ship arriving at Malyntaeas. Malazan patrols had to conducted by two squads at minimum for safety's sake.  As two-thirds of the occupying Malazan squads were about to leave with replacements uncertain, the situation in Malyntaeas looked to get very unsettled.
In
Return of the Crimson Guard
Hurl
remembered that
Rell
had been recruited from where he had lingered in a gaol in Malyntaeas.
In
Assail
Malyntaeas accents were amongst those heard by
Jute Hernan
from the stranded passengers and crew of the graveyard of ships on the north coast of the
Sea of Gold
.
History
The city's half-ruined Korhivi keep had been nearly destroyed when the Nathii had made war against the Korhivi.  A fleet of Nathii ships had filled the bay, flinging stones against the keep and surrounding walls.  The fighting had been so intense that neither side noticed the arrival of Malazan
High Fist
Dujek Onearm
with his three legions from the
Malaz 2nd Army
, the
Bridgeburners
, and two
High Mages
.  By day's end, the Nathii fleet had been sunk, the Genabarii royal had been killed in their red castle, and the Korhivi keep had surrendered.
A week before their march on the city of
Mott
, the
Malazan
Second
and
Third Armies
landed south of Malyntaeas and two days from the landing,
Fiddler
was introduced to
Moranth munitions
.

======================================================================
PAGE: Maurik
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Maurik
======================================================================

Map Genabackis published in MoI
The port city of
Maurik
was due north of
Coral
where the
River Maurik
entered the
Rust Ocean
. Its main thoroughfare ran west through town from the city harbour. The southern side of the street was occupied by squat, sprawling multi-story warehouses while the north side was occupied by civic buildings, trader shops, inns, and taverns. Hauling ropes from the upper floors of the warehouses crossed above the road to the flat roofs of the trader shops.
South of the warehouses ran the River Maurik, which was not navigable where it passed through the city.  The give and take between tide and current on the river resulted in ever changing sandbars that could only be cleared by the most shallow-draughted craft. Goods brought down the river had to be offloaded at the flats upriver and carted to the city's warehouses. Outside the city, the river was lined with ramshackle fisher huts and shacks on stilts.
Maurik was the first of several cities to be taken in the northward expansion of the
Pannion Domin
. The ruler of Maurik had capitulated to the Pannion invasion by arresting all of the city's priests and delivering them to the
Tenescowri
to be eaten. In return, she was granted a governorship by the
Pannion Seer
and was able to confiscate the wealth of the temples.
After the invasion, it became an empty city with all of its occupants being either mutilated, eaten, or kept to be devoured later. Its warehouses were stripped bare and a seastorm had filled the streets with toppled ornamental trees and seaweed-tangled sand dunes.
In
Memories of Ice
After the allied forces of
Caladan Brood
and
Dujek Onearm
defeated the army of
Septarch
Kulpath
and lifted the
Siege of Capustan
, they set their eyes on Coral. The armies split into two to liberate the cities of
Lest
and
Setta
before planning rejoin to at Maurik.
Brood's forces arrived first, and
Whiskeyjack
brought a portion of
Onearm's Host
down the Maurik River by barge from Setta. The rest were transported by
Quorl
closer to Coral. He was met outside the city by
Caladan Brood
,
Kallor
,
Hurlochel
,
Orfantal
, and
Korlat
who were eager to discover where
High Fist
Dujek Onearm
and the rest of the expected
Malazan
army had gone.
In
Toll the Hounds
A year after the Pannion Domin's downfall, Maurik remained a dead city.
Notes and references

======================================================================
PAGE: Mersin
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Mersin
======================================================================

Seven Cities
Mersin
was a city on
Seven Cities
. Once known as
Inath'an Merusin
, it was the only settlement remaining of the great cities that once lined the
Mersin River
.
Like the others, it had practised intensive irrigation techniques to flood the plains for agriculture and cleared the forests to harvest lumber for ships.  Eventually the river choked itself with silt and the topsoil of the
Lato Odhan
disappeared making the area unable to sustain a large population for thousands of years.
In
The Bonehunters
While travelling through the area,
Icarium
recalled Inath'an Merusin and the many other cities along the river.  He was shocked when
Mappo Runt
told him that most of the cities had long ago crumbled into ruin.  In fact, the amnesiac
Jhag
even failed to recall their last trip through the same region nearly eighty years earlier.
Trivia
Although spelled "Inath'an Merusin" in the text of
The Bonehunters
, the ancient city's name was spelled "Inath'an Mersin" in the book's glossary.

PAGE: Minikenar
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Minikenar
======================================================================

Seven Cities
Minikenar
was a once thriving city on the banks of a river, also long gone, west of
Y'Ghatan
on the
Seven Cities
sub-continent.  At the time of the
Malazan Empire
, only "a swath of potsherds reduced to gravel [...] remained".
During the time of the
First Empire
, the
T'rolbarahl
,
Dejim Nebrahl
, had hunted there for blood.
A once level road running east from the city, and south of the site of
Yadeth Garath
, had deteriorated into a crumbling track.
A string of fishing villages to Minikenar's north no longer displayed any signs of having ever existed.
In
The Bonehunters
After being driven away from a slave caravan by
Iskaral Pust
, Dejim Nebrahl had been unable to find food in the plague-ridden region.  Fevered and starved, the T'rolbarahl journeyed to Minikenar and other old hunting grounds hoping to find human prey.  He found only dust and memories.  A group of bedraggled
Malaz 14th Army
survivors of the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
, which included
Fiddler
and others, followed the Minikenar road hoping to catch up to
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
and the main force of the army.  They sent
Masan Gilani
ahead on their only horse  to speed their rescue.  Dejim Nebrahl attacked Gilani on the road before he himself was ambushed by the
Deragoth
and the
Hounds of Shadow
.

======================================================================
PAGE: Nathilog
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Nathilog
======================================================================

Map Genabackis from GotM
Nathilog
was a city on an island in the north-west of
Genabackis
. It was amongst the first of the northern Genabackis settlements to be
conquered
by the
Malazan Empire
.
Some
Malaz 2nd Army
soldiers involved in the
Siege of Pale
were veterans of the campaign there.
On the opposite side of the same island was the city of
Ayjhan
.
Pre-Malazan History
At one point, Nathilog was a fortress with ringed-round cyclopean walls, thick towers and deep donjons. During that time, a shipwrecked
Seguleh
was given a tour of its defenses to demonstrate that the place was impregnable. A detailed description of the encounter was given in
Sulerem of Mengal
's
Histories of Genabackis
.
Prior to the conquest by the Malazan Empire, Nathilog had been notorious as a haven for pirates ruled by self-styled barons.
This collection of barons may have been what
Crokus Younghand
once referred to as the "Nathilog Confederacy".
Presumably, an event known as the First Age of the
Nathilog Wars
took place here.
Quick Ben
said it occurred long before the Malazan Empire and involved the sorceress
Nightchill
.
The Malazan army, specifically the
Bridgeburners
, faced a coalition of the
Crimson Guard
,
Caladan Brood
,
Anomander Rake
and the
Tiste Andii
, the
Mott Irregulars
, and the Nathii First Army during the Blackdog campaigns.
Under Malazan rule
Nathilog became one of the main trading points for goods from Genabackis en route to
Quon Tali
. Its aristocracy was eventually completely Talianised.
Anomander Rake
thought the Malazan conquest of the city had been to its betterment.  He described the city as once being less even than the pre-conquest
Genabaris
, which he labelled a "fetid sore".  The Malazans had brought peace, reparation, law, and order.   Now both cities could claim rivalry to
Darujhistan
.
In
Orb Sceptre Throne
At the time of the rise of the
Jaghut Tyrant
in
Darujhistan
, Nathilog was in the care of governor
Agull'en
who resided in the hall of rulership originally used by the barons. He had a bodyguard of twenty
Barghast
and used a
Rhivi
shaman as a
mage
.
The self-styled
Legate
of Darujhistan sent an emissary to each of the ex-free cities, including Nathilog, to demand their governors' allegiance. The incredulous Agull'en pointed out that Darujhistan had no troops while the Malazans had thousands, then ordered the emissary flayed. It was likely Agull'en did not survive the emissary's response, which killed his guards and destroyed his ruling hall.
In
The God is Not Willing
In his
History of This and That
,
Brath of Worthless Ingot
recorded the arrival of the XXXI Legion in Nathilog from
Seven Cities
. The Legion was at barely two-thirds strength after a disastrous ocean crossing beset by unseasonal storms. Unsubstantiated rumours of the
Desert Plague
on board forced the local authorities to quarantine the fleet in the bay with fire-ship patrols. Morale amongst the Legion was dismal.
Stillwater
carried a five-lens eyeglass she had looted from Brightgo's Barrow outside Nathilog.
Amiss
recalled how
Storp
had almost died in a tunnel at Nathilog during the
Genabackis Campaign
while serving in the
sapper
auxiliary with the Bridgeburners.
Notable residents
Agull'en
- Malazan governor
Baedisk
- poet
Cracktooth Filcher
- scourge of cobblers
Notes and references
List of abbreviations
•
Paginations
•

CATEGORIES: Cities

Noh
and northeast of
Enjo Estarb

South Genabackis
New Landing
was the principle settlement of
Galatan Island
, which lay of the southern coast off
Genabackis
in the
Galatan Sweep
.  The city was on the western coast of the island and was likely a member of the
Confederacy of Free Cities
.  On the opposite end of the island was
Four Towers Ruins
.

Quon Tali
Nex
was a city in southern
Quon Tali
northeast of
Forest Horn
and
Fedal
. To the southeast were
Laeth
and
Ryns
.  To the northeast was
Ijor
.
History
Nex was one of the cities King
Chulalorn the Second
of
Kan
sought to subjugate as part of his attempt to resurrect the ancient kingdom of
Itko Kan
.  Chulalorn perished during his siege of the city after taking an arrow to the throat.

Nisst
was a city on the continent of
Genabackis
that was part of the alliance of
Free Cities
resisting the
Malazan Empire
's invasion of the continent.
It lay on a large inland lake along the River
Gan
.
Speculations
Based on a conversation between
Lorn
and
Dujek
, it seems likely that Nisst was listed as Ganiss on the map in
Gardens of the Moon
.

PAGE: Nita
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Nita
======================================================================

Quon Tali
Nita
was a city in northeastern
Quon Tali
. To its north was
Balstro
and to its south was
Unta
, the capital of the
Malazan Empire
.
Nita was a barony and was ruled by a baron or baroness.
Notable residents
Ranel
, baron
In
Kellanved's Reach
In the formative days of the
Malazan Empire
, Nita was an ally of
Malle of Gris
and was ruled by the young Baron
Ranel
. Malle thought that Ranel was a sullen "brat" and that there was reason to believe that he was not to be trusted. Therefore, Malle arranged for Ranel of Nita to be carefully watched.
Notable natives
Baron
Ranel

with
