Okan
was a city either of, or close to the region of
Kolanse
, most likely to the south, beyond what had been the forest of
Stet
.
In
Dust of Dreams
Starvers
and
Inquisitors
had marched on the city in the night, setting it ablaze and dragging its residents out of their homes to unspeakable fates.
Boneyards had ringed the city after the last of the livestock had been slaughtered.
Known residents
Visto

PAGE: Old Falar
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Old_Falar
======================================================================

Old Falar
was a city in mainland
Falar
located north of the
Great Fenn Range
and northwest of
Cabil
and
Belade
.
In
Forge of the High Mage
When nearby
Pull
and
Muheres
were threatened by the encroachment of the volcanic
The Mountain of Gold
,
Mallick Rel
casually dismissed the pleading for help from their citizens. He advised them to evacuate to
Belade
or Old Falar.
Speculations
Two maps of Falar are included in
Forge of the High Mage
.
Falair
appears as one of a handful of major cities on the "Central Malazan Empire" map in the front of the book, but not in the more detailed Falar & Environs map at the end of the book. 
It is possible that Falair (from the front map) and Old Falar (from the back map) are meant to be the same city as they roughly appear in the same area of both maps.

======================================================================
PAGE: Omari
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Omari
======================================================================

Seven Cities
Omari
[o-MAR-ee]
was an ancient city
along the
Vathar
river north of the
Vathar Forest
and south of the
Ugarat Odhan
in
Seven Cities
.
Notable residents
Septhune Anabhin
In
The Bonehunters
Omari was the westernmost of several ancient cities in the centre of the Seven Cities subcontinent that were home to a mostly subjugated people characterised by blonde hair, heart-shaped faces, and blue eyes.  It was implied they were the remnants of the original people of the
First Empire
as they shared these physical characteristics with the people of the
Kingdom of Lether
, a one-time First Empire colony.  Other cities whose populations included these remnant peoples were
Halaf
,
Guran
, and
Karashimesh
.
Trivia
Omari was one of many Seven Cities location names based on prehistoric dig sites that
Steven Erikson
pulled from one of his archaeology text books and moved around some of the letters.
Notes and references

•

PAGE: One Eye Cat
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/One_Eye_Cat
======================================================================

Map Genabackis from GotM
One Eye Cat
was one of the former
Free Cities
on the continent of
Genabackis
.
It was located inland, east of
Yend
and north of the
One Eye Mountains
on the shores of
Old King Lake
.
Notable residents
Galvas
- poet
Humble Measure
Nekath
- poet
Silken Glance
Sweetest Sufferance
History
During the
Malazan Empire
's
Genabackis Campaign
, the city allied with the
Crimson Guard
who left a company under
Jorrick Sharplance
to protect them. Once the Malazans laid siege to the city,
Humble Measure
's father conspired with Malazan agents to open the city gates under cover of night but was discovered and executed. The city
garrison
invaded the family's estate, raping and murdering Humble Measure's mother and half-sisters. Sharplance's Guard company took control of the remaining prisoners to prevent their slaughter and were expelled by the city's paranoid rulers. After the Guard departed, another conspiracy brought
Claw
assassins into the city for a bloody night of slaughter that led to the city's fall.

Northwest Genabackis
Map Genabackis from GotM
Oraz
was a city located in northwestern
Genabackis
. It lay to the west of
Mott
along the river leading from
Greydog Lake
to
Prospect Bay
.  Mott and Oraz were separated by the
Mott West Wood
and
Oraz Wood
.
The
Malazan Empire
conquered Oraz during the
Genabackis Campaign
before moving on to
Mott
.  It was
High Fist
Dujek Onearm
's attempt to secure his supply lines between Mott and Oraz that led to the
Mott Campaign
and resulted in the formation of the
Mott Irregulars
.

======================================================================
PAGE: Pale
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Pale
======================================================================

Map of Genabackis from GotM
Pale
was one of the
Free Cities
on the continent of
Genabackis
.
According to
Ganoes Paran
, it was about a thousand leagues from
Genabaris
although this may have been a figure of speech.
Tattersail
estimated Pale to be about three thousand leagues from
Unta
.
Many of the roofs were tiled
and the streets cobbled.
In what was likely the
Krael Quarter
, a maze of shanties and lean-tos crouched against the city walls.
The city had massive ancient stone walls, the foundations of which were built on a huge glacial dump which covered the entire valley area. Below the city walls this rock pile filled a giant crevice reaching so far underground that even with magic it was hardly possible to find its bottom.
Captain
Paran
's impression of Pale was that of a dying city as he observed the 'faded canopies over sagging balconies' indicating the 'bleached tints of long-lost glory'.
After the
Siege of Pale
, the streets were ill-lit. Whether this had always been the case was not made clear.
The people of Pale traditionally wore leggings and tunics, the exact appearance of which was not described.
Politics
Pale had a long-running and bloody history with the
Moranth
.
When the
Malazan Empire
advanced on the city, the mages of the city made an alliance with
Anomander Rake
.
Organizations
Vellum Makers' Guild
In
Gardens of the Moon
The Malazan Empire, under
High Fist
Dujek Onearm
, had laid siege to Pale for three years by the time the
Siege of Pale
ended in the late winter of 1163
rd
year of
Burn's Sleep
.
Once the city had been conquered, the Moranth were given an hour to take retribution, resulting in 18,739 people being killed, one for every Moranth confirmed as a victim of the trade war they had fought with the Free City.
Afterwards, the dead were cleared from the city and Malazan healers swept the city to eliminate the outbreak of plague and treat common ailments as part of the Empire's procedure to win over the commoners of the conquered populace. The nobility, however, faced a culling that may have seen as many as nine out of ten killed by public execution.
In
Memories of Ice
The city served as the base of operations for the now-renegade Dujek and his army. Tensions with the city's populace were high as the normal Malazan bureaucratic and financial controls exercised in conquered cities were outside the expertise of the conquering army.
In
The Bonehunters
After the
Siege of Coral
, half the
garrison
of Pale joined
Onearm's Host
to pacify the
Whirlwind
rebellion in
Seven Cities
.
In
Toll the Hounds
After
Humble Measure
and the surviving members of his household fled
One Eye Cat
, they followed the Rhivi Trail from
Patch
to Pale. They did not stay long before the Malazan Empire began the Siege of Pale, and they joined the other refugees fleeing to Darujhistan.
In
Return of the Crimson Guard
It was fashionable for wealthy
Untan
households to employ emigrants and refugees of the Imperial conquests as servants in their households. After Pale's fall, its citizens could be found in the Imperial capital working in their traditional garb.
In
Orb Sceptre Throne
Malazan troops maintained a garrison at Pale that served as the headquarters of
Fist
K'ess
.  When Darujhistan's new
Legate
demanded Pale's allegiance and the expulsion of the Malazan occupiers, the citizenry of Pale were quick to comply.
Beseiged in their burning garrison by crowds of rioters, the Malazans were forced to fight their way out of the city.
Known locations in Pale
Barracks
Eltrosan Square
Knobb's Inn
Krael Quarter
North gate
North Market Round
Old Palace
Opal Quarter
Vimkaros Inn
Notes and references

PAGE: Paliss
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Paliss
======================================================================

Korel,
aka
Lands of Fist
Paliss
was a large inland city and the capital of the Kingdom of
Rool
. It was there at the city's fortress that "Overlord"
Yeull 'ul Taith
installed himself.
The city was home to the Prioress, the nation's chief religious authority in the worship of
The Lady
, and the High Assessor, the nation's chief legal authority.
The city's Tabernacle of Our Lady was one of the two most revered holy sites on the
Island of Fist
.
Below the city's fortress was a network of tunnels dating back to before the city's founding.

======================================================================
PAGE: Pan'potsun
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Pan'potsun
======================================================================

Seven Cities subcontinent
Pan'potsun
was one of the
Holy Cities
of
Seven Cities
.
It was situated on the northeastern coast of the subcontinent.
History
It was there that the mage,
Hairlock
joined the
Malaz 2nd Army
's
mage cadre
after the
Siege of Aren
.
In
House of Chains
During the
Whirlwind
rebellion, several hundred
Malazans
from Pan'potsun,
G'danisban
, and
Ehrlitan
, had fled to the mountain fortress,
B'ridys
, southwest of G'danisban. There they were besieged by the people of G'danisban.
In
The Bonehunters
Cutter
,
Heboric
,
Scillara
,
Felisin Younger
, and
Greyfrog
passed through the city on their way from
Raraku
to
Otataral Island
. They were forced to sell their horses there for food and supplies.
In
No Life Forsaken
Steven Erikson's hand drawn map of Pan'potsun environs at the time of
No Life Forsaken
High Fist
Jalan Arenfall
told
Hasten Thenu
of a curious woman he had encountered some five years after the events of
The Crippled God
. The High Fist was performing at a tavern in Pan'potsun, playing
He Who Fell Shall Rise
, a poem of
Fisher kel Tath
's that he had set to music. During the performance, a Pardu woman in her late thirties or early forties with a tattoo of a broken chain had sat at one of the tables and a crowd seemed to gather about her. She seemingly was familiar with the poem, because during a long instrumental before the final stanza she rose and began to dance. The combination of her transcendent dance and Arenfell's music broke the crowd. Arenfall was broken as well, but by the time he thought to look for the woman, she was gone. hasten Thenu knew the woman to be
Lostara Yil
.
While talking of
Dessimbelackis
' hubris in naming his nation the
First Empire
,
Mael
noted that a lost and forgotten civilization had built an underground waterway linking Pan'potsun with Ehrlitan long before the First Empire existed.
Trivia
When asked by a fan whether the name "Pan'potsun" was meant to invoke "pots and pans", author
Steven Erikson
said the name was actually "a riff on an archaeological site".

Seven Cities
Pur Atrii
was a city
in the northern portion of the continent of
Seven Cities
.  It was to the north of
Raraku
and to the west of
Kansu
.
In
The Bonehunters
As
Leoman
and the remnants of the
Army of the Whirlwind
fled the
Battle of Raraku
, a natural dust storm provided cover for their escape.  An arm of the storm blew all the way to Pur Atrii.
In
Reaper's Gale
The
Third Edur Imperial Fleet
menaced the waters of northern Seven Cities searching for champions to face Emperor
Rhulad Sengar
and capturing natives they thought might provide valuable intelligence. Among those they took back to
Letheras
with them were a number of denizens of Pur Atrii.

PAGE: Quaint
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Quaint
======================================================================

Quaint
was a high walled city-state located on the shore of a peninsula far from its neighbors.
Until recently it had been ruled by the vicious and corrupt
King Necrotus
the Nihile.  Now his body was one of the corpses that hung upside-down on the city's inland wall.
Quaint's new ruler was Necrotus' brother,
King Macrotus
the Overwhelmingly Considerate.  Macrotus was obsessed with health and purity and so made worship of the
Lady of Beneficence
the state's sole legal religion.  He banished the court's mages and raised and an army of
Well Knights
whose purpose was to enforce volumes of new prohibitions covering all aspects of life designed to promote the populace's health.  All vices were forbidden, diets were made vegetarian, exercise was mandatory, public displays of emotion were prohibited, babies were not allowed to disturb the peace with their cries, and so on.  Every citizen's duty was to die healthy.  Those that failed had their corpses hung upside-down from the city walls.
The royal palace featured a long colonnade lined with upright glass lidded coffins displaying the agonized expressions of those citizens — known as the "Healthy Dead" — who had died in healthy prescribed manners.  It also contained a room-sized mechanism designed by the king to exercise his muscles and joints for half of every day.
The city's religious life centered around the Grand Temple of the Lady, who was said to dwell in a pit at its center.
Its formal front entrance featured a blockish altar sitting atop a raised platform from whence the Lady's voice could periodically be heard making pronouncements.  Its operations were run by veiled nuns and priestesses.
Notable Residents
Agin Again
- Demoness of Lust
Arpo Relent
- Well Knight
Elas Sil
- Saint of Glorious Labor
Imid Factallo
- Saint of Glorious Labor

- Demon of Vice

- Well Knight, Purest of Paladins

- Demon of Corpulence

- Demoness of Sloth

Spoiler warning
:
The following section contains significant plot details about Quaint.
In
The Healthy Dead
Dissatisfied Saints,
Imid Factallo
and
Elas Sil
, hired the necromancers,
Bauchelain
and
Korbal Broach
, to depose the tyrannical King Macrotus who was killing his subjects with kindness.
The necromancers sowed chaos by raising the city's dead while their manservant,
Emancipor Reese
, subverted the city's leading paladin,
Invett Loath
.
Bauchelain brought Macrotus's rule to an end when he revealed the king had died and that his healthy agenda had been run in league with
Agin Again
, the Demoness of Lust.  The necromancer designated Imid Factallo and Elas Sil as the new king and queen of Quaint.
Significant plot details  end here.

Quon Tali by
Joshua Butler
Quon Tali
[KWAN TAL-ee]
was the home
continent
of the
Malazan Empire
.
It was bounded to the south and west by the
Horn Ocean
. To the southeast lay
Reacher's Ocean
and to the east, the
Falari
and
Bloor Seas
. In the north lay the
Ice Fields
and to the northeast, the
Colonnus Sea
.
To the southeast were the islands of
Geni
,
Kartool
,
Malaz
, and
Nap
. The mysterious drifting island of
Drift Avalii
lay somewhere to the southwest of the continent.
The ancient
Trunk Road
crossed the continent's midsection connecting the cities of
Quon Tali
,
Li Heng
, and
Unta
.
History
Unofficial Malaz World Map by D'rek
The history of the continent was dominated by two rival provinces, Unta in the east and Quon Tali in the west.  Each sought to dominate trade and crush its rival while "lesser states,
Itko Kan
,
Cawn
,
Gris
, and
Dal Hon
, danced in a myriad of alliances, trade combines and Troikas marshaled against one or both poles."  When the Malazans began their domination of the continent, Unta and Quon Tali were the first to fall.
After sealing the deal with Kellanved, the province's council of nobles was rounded up and beheaded.
According to the Seer
Rigga
, the Quon Tali province of Itko Kan had been under Malazan occupation for about a hundred years by 1161
BS
. It used to be an independent country with its own banner.
It was believed by Malazan scholars, that the use and manufacturing of iron tools and weapons had only occurred in the last 500 years on the Quon Tali continent.  Before that, the people had used bronze.

Purage

Geography

PAGE: Quon Tali (city)
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Quon_Tali_(city)
======================================================================

Quon Tali
Quon Tali
was a city and province
on the western coast of the continent of the same name,
Quon Tali
.
The city was formed of two neighbouring sister cities originally known as
Quon
and
Tali
.
The city lay on the western terminus of the ancient
Trunk Road
trade route which crossed the continuent to
Li Heng
and
Unta
.
Tali was a "sprawling collection of distinct precincts and quarters".
Quon Talians were characterised by olive skin.
History
In the distant past, Quon and Tali had both been independent and heavily fortified cities. At this time, the Talians had - every few years - besieged Quon.
Subsequently, Quon and Tali became powerful allied city-states, led by kings.
They were, however, finally conquered by the
Malazan Empire
. In the intervening centuries, the twin cities had warred with the
Seti
and had sent their
Iron Legions
along the Trunk Road to subjugate the lands of the east.
Periodically, they successfully controlled much of the continent under what was known as the Quon Tali Hegemony/Talian Hegemony.
When the Malazans conquered Quon Tali, the ruling
Tayliin
family were tracked down and essentially exterminated by the
Claw
.
While still under self-rule, Quon Tali's official colours had been dark blue instead of Malazan grey.
Notable Quon Talians
Carlat
Dancer
Dorin Rav
Faruj
Ghelel Rhik Tayliin
Imogan
Pearl
(a merchant of Quon)
Commander
Renquill
In
Return of the Crimson Guard
During the Malazan civil war, a troika of Talian noble families seized control of the city from
Fist
Kal'il
and ejected the Malazan garrison.  Military command fell to
Old Guard
member, General
Choss
, as part of the
Talian League
.
In
Kellanved's Reach
When Quon and Tali were still twin city-states - separate entities connected by an 'alliance' - their relationship could be summarized by an "old saying":
"Quon pays so that Tali can fight"
. This meant that when Quon was being threatened by forces from their long-time enemy,
Nom Purge
, that the military might of Tali was obligated to come to the aid of Quon.
Tali was located further inland than Quon, and unlike Quon, Tali was still heavily fortified with strong, intact walls. Tali was characterized by "towers and enclosed baileys" so as to form layers of defense - which contributed to the city's general feeling of confinement. At this particular time, the majority of the military resources of Tali were involved in an all-out offensive on Nom Purge and on the city of
Purage
to the north.
Quon, on the other hand, occupied gentle hills overlooking the extensive waterfront and warehouse district, which together, contributed significantly to Quon being the "richest western port of the continent
Quon Tali
". Quon was "expansive and rambling" and characterized by many large family estates of the various trading houses, as well as by a number of city squares devoted to markets of a wide variety of superior goods. Unfortunately, Quon - lulled by the existence of the alliance with Tali - had carelessly allowed the removal of many of the stones of its northern wall, leaving just ragged remnants of a wall what had once been "formidable and thick". Because of this, Quon was vulnerable to the entry of the forces of Nom Purge, who took advantage of this weakness to enter the city and burn down the warehouse district.

Seven Cities
Subcontinent
Rang
was the outermost city on the long
Maadil Peninsula
dividing the
Kokakal Sea
and the
Maadil Sea
on the
Seven Cities
subcontinent. Across the water to the east was the island city of
Kaliban
. To Rang's south lay
Taxila
.
Language
The architect
Taxilian
from Taxila mentioned a nearly extinct language called tribal
Rangala
, which was spoken by just himself and his grandfather's sister. One can presume, this language had something to do with the region of the city of Rang, just north of Taxila itself.

PAGE: Reliant City
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Reliant_City
======================================================================

Reliant City
was the starting point for pilgrims travelling the
Cracked Pot Trail
, a cobblestoned pilgrim's pathway from the Gates of Nowhere to the Shrine of the
Indifferent God
in
Farrog
.  It lay on the edge of the
Great Dry
, a large plateau of scrub grass and rocks.  Finders camped at the trails start to guide pilgrims.
The city maintained a community of artists who often made the long trek to Farrog to participate in that city's annual performance contest.
One of its most venerable groups were the Dantocs.  It was not revealed if this was a family name or title.
Notable residents
Calap Roud
Dantoc Calmpositis
Mister Must Ambertroshin

PAGE: Ring
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Ring
======================================================================

Korel,
aka
Lands of Fist
Ring
was a large walled city located along the eastern border of the Empire of
Jourilan
where the Lesser White River flowed into the
Flow Strait
and the
Blight Sea
. Its name was probably derived from the
Ring Wall
which lay almost directly north of the city.
It was some hundred times the size of the city of
Blight
.  From the hills overlooking the city an observer could see red and black tiled rooftops and towers as well as a tall bell tower and chapel of
the Lady
.  The Cathedral of Our Lady stood in a broad open plaza, wide steps leading to its tall oaken doors.
In
Stonewielder
The fields outside the city were the site of the final battle between the Jourilan Empire and the
Jourilan Army of Reform
.  Imperial Prince
Ranur
brought his
Heavy cavalry
and
Jasston
and
Dourkan
mercenaries against some fifty thousand peasant troops led by Commander
Martal
and
Ivanr
the Deliverer. The city itself burned in places as Reformist and Loyalist factions fought for control of precincts.
The Reformists weathered a series of devastating charges before the tide of battle turned in their favour.  Even a contingent of several thousand Ring citizens joined the battle's final moments.  Afterwards the Reformists turned on the city's Loyalists, massacring them in the streets.
Stormguard
from the garrison on
Ring Wall
came to the Cathedral of Our Lady to protect the families hidden inside.
In one final act of destruction, a massive tidal wave destroyed the city's docks and swept into the city.  When it withdrew, it took countless souls with it.

PAGE: Rutu Jelba
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Rutu_Jelba
======================================================================

Seven Cities
Subcontinent
Rutu Jelba
was a port city in northern
Otataral Island
on the
Seven Cities
subcontinent. It was located on a narrow isthmus between the
Otataral
and
Talgai Seas
.
Fiddler
described it as a lizard-infested, orange-bricked cesspool.
The city was a primary destination for
Tanno
pilgrims from Seven Cities. Tanno
Drakes
brought pilgrims to the city under the protection of a
Spiritwalker
or
Mendicant
.
A pilgrim trail led from the city through the
Talgai Mountains
to the
Holy City
of
Karakarang
.
The city's people were known as the
Jelban
.
In
Deadhouse Gates
Fiddler,
Kalam
,
Crokus
, and
Apsalar
passed through the city on their way from
Darujhistan
to
Itko Kan
via the Seven Cities subcontinent.
In
The Bonehunters
Taxilian
fled the
Bluetongue Plague
by taking a drake bound for Rutu Jelba. Two days from their destination they were attacked by the
Third Edur Imperial Fleet
.
Some time afterwards, the Tanno Spiritwalkers placed Otataral Island under self-imposed isolation. Once the plague was broken, they lifted the order and merchants from Rutu Jelba made their way to the mainland. They brought basic staples to trade, but found mostly empty villages.
Cutter
,
Barathol Mekhar
,
Scillara
, and
Chaur
encountered Jelban traders somewhere in eastern Seven Cities as the made their way to the western coast of the
Otataral Sea
.

PAGE: Saltoan
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Saltoan
======================================================================

Fan made map of Saltoan, based on descriptions, by
Jacob Gamm
"
The city is Hood's crusted navel incarnate. I wouldn't take Rallick Nom's axe-wielding mother to Saltoan.
"
―
Coll
Saltoan
was one of the oldest cities on the
Vision Plain
. It was located in the eastern part of the continent of
Genabackis
on the trader road between
Darujhistan
and
Capustan
. It was surrounded by thick low walls stained with brown streaks. No guards monitored traffic passing through the huge wooden doors of the city's gates. Having sent its vaunted
Horse Guard
to join
Caladan Brood
's Host, the city became a mostly lawless place with its pitiful constabulary no match for the various thieving groups vying to control the city.
"
Saltoan had once stood alongside the river
Catlin
, growing rich on the cross-continent trade, until the river changed its course in the span of a single, rain-drenched spring. Korselan's Canal was built in an effort to re-establish the lucrative link with the river trade, as well as four deep lakes - two within the old river bed itself - for moorage and berths. The effort had seen only marginal success, and the four hundred years since that time had witnessed a slow, inexorable decline.
"
―Description of Saltoan
The city was characterised by crumbling architecture, and narrow alleyways through rat-infested tenements. The streets stank of rotting rubbish and sewage.
Although nominally ruled by a king and council, true power was said to belong to the city's hold-masters and mistresses, local crimelords who each controlled their own territory.
The roads leading away from the city were monitored by spotters at the city gates who could report particularly promising caravans to the local bandits.
Notable residents
Garno
, hold-master
Kenth
, assassin
Nektara
, hold-mistress
Points of interest
Korselan's Canal
Mucosin Street
Sunrise Gate
Sunset Gate
Twistface Passage
Waytown, a small settlement just outside the Sunrise Gate
Wu's Closet Square
In
Memories of Ice
Genabackis
As the
Pannion Domin
expanded its influence to the northwest, Pannion priests began proselytizing in the city for the cult. They promised the return of law and order, threatening the rule of the city's crimelords. The merchant
Keruli
travelled to the city with
Gruntle
,
Stonny Menackis
, and
Harllo
as his bodyguards. He met with the local thieving guilds to relay the true horrors of the cult and to explain their use of disinformation and discord to conquer their enemies. He convinced them that counter-intelligence was a more effective response than violence.
For four days, the city was the site of a series of unexplained murders. This occurred during the same time period that the necromancers,
Bauchelain
and
Korbal Broach
, were in the area.
After the
Siege of Capustan
, a regiment of Saltoan cavalry was listed among the ranks of
Caladan Brood
's forces as they made their way to face the
Pannion Seer
at
Coral
.
In
Toll the Hounds
A
spokesman
for the pilgrims of the
Pilgrim camp
surrounding the
Barrow of the Redeemer
recalled his time as a refugee in Saltoan. He had been a wealthy merchant in Capustan before fleeing to Saltoan ahead of the Pannion Domin's army. In Saltoan, he had witnessed the Expulsion--the night when the advance agents of Pannion Domin were driven out of the city.
The nomadic tyrant of the
Lamatath Plain
known as
The Captain
sent emissaries to Saltoan and other cities bordering the plain to announce his claim to the territory.

PAGE: Sarn
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Sarn
======================================================================

Map Genabackis published in MoI
Sarn
had one-time been a sizeable city
within the territory of the
Pannion Domin
. Now the few that still lived there hacked away at the hard ground trying to cultivate land that had been fallow for far too long.
Sarn was located to the west of
Pilgrim Lake
and to the east of
Bastion
. A well-made cobbled and guttered road connected it to nearby Bastion,
Kel Tor
, and
Heath
.
The road near the city had once been settled all along its length with ribbon farms set behind stalls, shops, and taverns.
In
Toll the Hounds
Like other settlements of the former Pannion Domin, Sarn was said to have begun to regain prosperity through the production of
Kelyk
, which it sent to Bastion for distribution.
Nimander Golit
,
Aranatha
,
Desra
,
Kedeviss
,
Skintick
left
Morsko
and travelled near Sarn with a comatose
Clip
towards Bastion.
They found the few residents left were impoverished and skittish as dogs, dropping their hoes and running at the
Tiste Andii
's approach.
The nomadic tyrant of the
Lamatath Plain
known as
The Captain
was apparently unaware of Sarn's diminished status. He sent emissaries to Sarn and other "cities" bordering the plain to announce his claim to the territory.

Seven Cities, area north of Aren
Seven Cities
Sarpachiya
was a major city
on the
River Ugarat
north of the
Clatar Sea
on
Seven Cities
.  The river originated in the
Thalas Mountains
and ran roughly north-south, passing through
Ugarat
before reaching Sarpachiya.  Further downriver was
T'sarech
and
Nahal
.
In
House of Chains
Karsa Orlong
exited
Omtose Phellack
in the
Jhag Odhan
.  On the far eastern horizon, he could make out a city and the glimmer of a vast river.  He surmised that the city was Sarpachiya.

======================================================================
PAGE: Sepik
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Sepik
======================================================================

Seven Cities
Sepik
was a city, island, and kingdom of the same name located in the
Sepik Sea
northwest of the
Seven Cities
subcontinent. To the island's north was the
Dryjhna Ocean
and to its southwest was the nation of
Nemil
. To the northeast was the island city of
Monkan
.
The Sepik Kingdom was an Imperial principality and a remote protectorate of the
Malazan Empire
.
The relationship between Sepik and the Malazan Empire came about because the benign-ruling
King of Sepik
had been clever enough to send representatives to
Kellanved
, the Malazan emperor, proposing conditions of surrender rather than waiting to be conquered.
The Emperor had simply accepted, making Sepik a vassal of his Empire.
It was likely no one from the Malazan Empire had ever visited the place.
There were two distinct populations making up the inhabitants of Sepik — one subject to the other.
The indigenous people, actually of mixed
Tiste Edur
derivation, had long been subjugated, enslaved, and degraded by the
Humans
. This Edur underclass were called "Rulhun'tal ven'or" or the 'Mudskins' (because of their characteristically Tiste Edur greyish skin).
The city of Sepik was tucked into a halfmoon bay, beyond which were upland villages.
In
The Bonehunters
Samar Dev
pointed out Sepik to
Karsa Orlong
as a point of interest when the
Teblor
pored over her collection of maps in her workshop in
Ugarat
.  When he heard the island held a population of slaves, the scowling Karsa determined to go there.
The two travelled as far as the
Olphara Peninsula
before their encounter with a portion of the
Third Edur Imperial Fleet
led by
Hanradi Khalag
superseded their original plans.
The fleet had been sent to the other side of the world by
Rhulad Sengar
, the Tiste Edur emperor of the
Letherii Empire
, to murder and terrorise the people of Seven Cities.
Another portion of the
Tiste Edur
fleet led by
Tomad Sengar
made landfall at Sepik where they unexpectedly found the enslaved class of mixed-blood Edur. Tomad's Edur warriors and
Letherii
marines "liberated" their degenerate cousins and brought them back to their ships to serve their new masters.
Then they penned the humans of Sepik, forcing mothers to cast their babies and children into a bonfire. Afterwards, the women were raped and beheaded while the men were forced to watch before being dismembered themselves.  The wailing grey-haired King of Sepik was the last to die.  He was flung from a tower after being forced to watch his cherished subjects tortured and murdered, and he met his death with relief.
Nearby Monkan met a similar fate.
Admiral
Nok
's Malazan Imperial Fleet transporting
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
's
14th Army
attempted to dock at Sepik to resupply, but found the city full only of the rotting dead.  The initial landing party disturbed tens of thousands of feasting gulls, crows, and island vultures that had gathered there.
Fiddler
thought the attack on a Malazan protectorate meant war with the Edur if Empress
Laseen
desired it.
The Edur fleet eventually brought their distant Edur kin, the 'Mudskins', back to
Letheras
.
In
Reaper's Gale
The Edur brought their miserable Sepik prisoners back to Letheras, although a dozen did not survive the trip and were kept stacked in a ship's hold encased in wax.
The rest Tomad Sengar relegated to the city's trench-pens, chained alongside debtors, traitors, and murderers, where they died in droves while he attempted to meet with Emperor Rhulad to decide on their final disposition. Tomad found the Sepik half-breeds pathetic mockeries of the Tiste Edur and cared little for their fate. Chancellor
Triban Gnol
prevented Tomad from meeting with Rhulad to drive a wedge between them, then carefully broached the subject of the forgotten Edur kin to stoke the Emperor's anger. Rhulad ordered his parents brought before him for their cruel treatment of the Sepik and ordered Tomad and Uruth to be punished in a similar manner. They were sentenced to be chained in dungeon crypt of the
Eternal Domicile
's Fifth Wing for two months.
The freed Sepik were emaciated, nearly naked, and covered with welts and sores. They gathered outside the Champion's Quarters where
Karsa Orlong
resided and crowded around him when he appeared. Karsa spoke to them offering them nothing but an exhortation to accept their freedom.
Bugg
took pity on them and drew upon the power of
Denaeth Rusen
to send them away to the islands where he and
Tehol Beddict
resettled the city's other refugees.
At the same time, Adjunct Tavore cited the massacre at Sepik as one of the reasons the Bonehunters followed the Edur back to
Lether
to overthrow the Letherii Empire.

PAGE: Setta
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Setta
======================================================================

Map showing the spread of the Pannion Domin.
The empty city of
Setta
was located at the northern tip of the
Pannion Domin
's territory, south-west of
Lest
, and due east of the
Vision Mountains
. It lay on the banks of the
Setta River
, from which the city took its name, and which flowed to the
Rust Ocean
near Lest.
The
Maurik River
also passed close by on its way to the
city
of the same name.  It was larger in size than
Capustan
.
Setta was larger than
Capustan
.
The city had been annexed by the Pannion Domin forces under the command of
Septarch
Kulpath
. It took three weeks to beat back the city's defenders who presented a unified and well organised front, but who were ultimately no match for the Domin's sheer numbers.
Lest and Setta were producers of fine silks of pale yellow.
Quick Ben
referred to a saltworm that proliferated within the mines of the dry seabeds of Setta. They were long, thin, and red as blood with ridges and leg-like cilia along their length. They were able to turn the hardest pan of clay into sand and bred like maggots.
In
Memories of Ice
Captain
Ganoes Paran
and the
Bridgeburners
were the first outsiders to visit Setta after it had fallen to the Pannion Domin. Arriving by
Quorl
in the dark, they found the city empty but for feast-piles of human bone and ash left by the
Tenescowri
in the city's squares. There were also large nests atop the city's four towers where the
Pannion Seer
's
condor
servants bedded for the night.
High Fist
Dujek Onearm
's army passed by Setta on its way to Maurik where it was to reunite with
Caladan Brood
's allied army.
In
Toll the Hounds
A year after the Pannion Domin's downfall, Setta remained a dead city.
Notes and references

Among the silks the man recognised the dyed lavender twists and bolts of
Illem
, the pale yellows of Setta and Lest - two cities to the southeast he knew had been annexed by the
Pannion Seer
in the last month - and the heavy bold twists of
Sarokalle
.

PAGE: Seven Cities
CATEGORIES: Continents
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Seven_Cities

Seven Cities
Seven Cities
was a
sub-continent
north of
Quon Tali
and west of
Genabackis
that had been conquered by the
Malazan Empire
. It was an ancient land, built upon the ruins of countless cities dating back to the
First Empire
. Hot, dry, and largely desert, its sands obscured forgotten pathways, hoarded power, and soaked up sorcery. Every foot of the land had been walked by
Ascendants
.
Unofficial Malaz World Map by D'rek
History
Bronze Age
The subcontinent of Seven Cities was the birthplace of the human
First Empire
under Emperor
Dessimbelackis
.
Malazan Conquest of Seven Cities
Dassem Ultor, main commander responsible for the conquest of Seven Cities (by
Shadaan
)
The subcontinent of Seven Cities had been invaded and conquered by the Malazan Empire during the reign of
Emperor Kellanved
, under
First Sword
Dassem Ultor
and his generals, including
Whiskeyjack
,
Dujek Onearm
,
Korbolo Dom
,
Cartharon Crust
, and others. It is uncertain the exact year that the Malazan invasion began or how long the Malazans held Seven Cities by the time of the main series.
T'lan Imass rising from dust (by
McDev
)
During the conquest, both sides had access to vital magical assets. The Malazans possessed control over the army of the
Logros T'lan Imass
, powerful undead warriors with supernatural abilities and no limitations of a mortal army. Kellanved was constrained in deploying the
T'lan Imass
during the conquest, making use of them only when necessary.
On the other hand, Seven Cities forces had access to
otataral
, a local anti-magic substance that caused difficulties for Malazan mages until the T'lan Imass became more involved in the conquest. It was
Leoman
's belief that the invasion would have failed early on due to otataral if not for the T'lan Imass.
Following the conquest of the
Otataral Island
, the empire monopolized all otataral production to keep the substance within its sole control, operating slave
mining camps
like
Skullcup
where prisoners of war and political exiles were sentenced.
Ugarat by
Shadaan
Aren
was conquered early in the campaigns; following its occupation, Dassem Ultor commissioned the
Aren Way
as a military road.
At the holy city of
Ubaryd
, the Malazan
Claw
infiltrated the palace of the ruling
Falah'd
ahead of the army, brutally mutilating her until Dassem arrived and granted a merciful death, thus capturing the city.
The Falah'd of
Ehrlitan
,
Yathengar 'ul Amal
, was captured alive upon the conquest of his city and given a life sentence in the otataral mine called
the Pit
.
When Dassem's forces approached the holy city of
Ugarat
(famed as the center of classical learning in Seven Cities), the Falah'd
Enqura
ordered the destruction of the hundred-thousand scrolls of Ugarat and the murder of all scholars and teachers to deny the Malazans access to the city's knowledge. Countless works dating back to the First Empire were lost, and the name "Enqura" became a curse among both Malazans and Seven Cities natives.
In the 1147th Year of Burn's Sleep, Dassem Ultor fought a difficult campaign against three entire nomadic tribes while holding a vastly numerically inferior army. In response, he formulated a new doctrine allowing the Malazans to overcome the nightly raiding tactics of the nomads and defeat them.
First Rebellion of Seven Cities
By around the 1152nd - 1154th years of Burn's Sleep,
an abortive Seven Cities uprising that began in Aren was put down, and culminated in the decisive conquest of the entire subcontinent. In those years, several events coincided to bring a decisive end to whatever independence may have still existed in Seven Cities:
Kimloc, responsible for the surrender of Karakarang (by
Peter Jay
)
Bridgeburner emblem (by
YoltonsArt
)
Dassem Ultor's Siege of Y'ghatan (by Steven Erikson)
The
crushing
of the rebellious city of Aren by the Logros T'lan Imass, ending in an infamous slaughter of the city (unusual conduct for the T'lan Imass up to that stage in the campaign); the peaceful surrender of the Holy City of
Karakarang
upon negotiations between Dujek Onearm and
Kimloc
, leader of the
Tano
cult, to avoid Aren's fate;
a successful campaign in the
Pan'potsun Odhan
by Dassem Ultor, ending in him personally slaying a Holy
Falah'd
; Whiskeyjack's scouring of the holy desert
Raraku
and his victory against the rebel Seven Cities
mage cabal
, leading to the birth of the
Bridgeburners
and their legend, as well as the recruitment of
Kalam
and
Quick Ben
;
and the
Siege of Y'Ghatan
, which broke the last active insurrectionist elements of Seven Cities at the cost of the near-razing of the city and the deaths of 8,000-10,000 Malazan soldiers,
and which culminated in the death of Dassem Ultor.
Shortly after the Siege of Y'Ghatan and Dassem Ultor's death, Emperor Kellanved was assassinated and
Empress Laseen
was enthroned in his stead. Whiskeyjack was soon demoted and replaced by Dujek Onearm, whereupon the two generals and their forces were transferred over to the
new campaign
on the continent of
Genabackis
. Seven Cities supplied the front lines for the Malazan campaign on Genabackis,
and most of the Malazan soldiers on Genabackis were of Seven Cities origin.
The Logros refused to acknowledge the ascension of the new Empress and marched into the
Jhag Odhan
west of Seven Cities to fight the
28th Jaghut War
against a newly discovered Jaghut enclave; of the 19,000 T'lan Imass, only 14,000 returned.
Cartharon Crust was appointed the Malazan
High Fist
of Aren following the pacification, with overall command over all of Seven Cities. Some years following Laseen's enthronement, Cartharon drowned in the Aren harbour under suspicious circumstances, soon joined by his brother
Urko
. His high command was replaced by High Fist
Pormqual
around the 1160th year of Burn's Sleep. High Fist Pormqual was an incompetent, inattentive, and effete administrator that largely left governance to wealthy merchant interests. In particular, Pormqual's chief advisor was
Mallick Rel
, a
Jhistal
priest with significant influence over the Aren court.
Second Rebellion of Seven Cities
See also:
Whirlwind Rebellion
Cities
Fan made Seven Cities map by
Joshua Butler
Holy Cities
The Holy Cities from which the sub-continent gained its name were said to have been founded by seven Ascendants thousands of years ago.
Before the Malazan conquest, each city was ruled by a
Holy Falah'd
.
The holy "Seven Cities" were:
Aren
Ehrlitan
Karakarang
Karashimesh
Ubaryd
Ugarat
Yath Alban
The most devout pilgrims pursued the Path of the Seven, a journey to each of the Holy Cities. Pilgrimage was a respected activity and was a tradition unphased by bandits or war.
Other cities
Other cities named as Holy Cities included
G'danisban
,
Hissar
,
Lothal
,
Mersin
,
Pan'potsun
,
and
Y'Ghatan
.
Lost cities included
Hedori Kwil
,
Kanarbar Belid
,
Minikenar
,
N'karaphal
,
Tramara
,
Trebur
,
Vinith
,
Vithan Taur
, and
Yadeth Garath
.
Geography
To the northwest it was bounded by the
Sepik Sea
and the
Dryjhna Ocean
. To the north, by the
Kokakal
,
Maadil
,
Talgai
,
Otataral
, and
Bandiko Seas
, as well as the
Sea of Kaltepe Kadesh
. To the east were the
Sea of Gallada
, the
Sahul
and
Dojal Hading Seas
, and
Seeker's Deep
. To the south lay the
Cragg Sea
and
Quon Tali
. The
Clatar Sea
was contained within the south-central portion of the continent itself.
Whiskeyjack
commented that
Mock's Hold
(to the southeast of mainland Quon Tali) was about 3000 leagues from Seven Cities.

Customs
Seven Cities by Werthead
Beliefs and practices
Seven Cities superstition held that the loss of an eye was also the birth of inner sight.
According to
Duiker
, the saying "Every meal is your last" encompassed an entire Seven Cities philosophy.
Children partook in "the naming rite" where family spoke for them and gave them their names. For this reason orphaned children often had no names.
If a loved one were to die far from home, the corpse might be left pinned beneath a heavy stone to prevent its discovery by wandering spirits. The ground would then be hallowed by spitting in eight directions, spilling drops of blood on the stone from the left hand, and voicing blessings in the name of the Apocalyptic.
All the oldest legends of
dragons
in Seven Cities started by saying that they were the essence of sorcery.
Gestures and militancy
The traditional Seven Cities way to challenge an opponent was to spit on the floor in front of him. When so provoked by
Hairlock
,
Tayschrenn
told the mage from Seven Cities that his primitive tribal gestures remained quaint, if somewhat tasteless.
When
Toc the Younger
spat past the left ear of his horse,
Captain Paran
shivered at the thought that in the old days, this gesture would have announced the beginning of tribal war among the Seven Cities. He also thought that the gesture had become the symbol of the
Malaz 2nd Army
.
Ganoes Paran
thought that the natives of Seven Cities had a predisposition for causing trouble and attributed the problems of the
Genabackis Campaign
to the pre-dominance of Seven Cities natives in the Malazan
2nd
,
5th
, and
6th Armies
.
Tools and architecture
The
long-knife
was the weapon of choice among Seven Cities warriors.
It was common for Seven Cities market streets to be topped by tarps slung between buildings. This created a tunnel effect and likely reduced the heat of the sun.
Seven Cities pottery was more elegant than its Malazan equivalent. Its shapes were elongated with cream or white glazing on necks and rims and faded red on the body. It was decorated with full-toned and realistic images.
In
Gardens of the Moon
,
Paran
used a Seven Cities-style saddle which was high-backed with a hinged horn that folded forward.
One common form of architecture found scattered across Seven Cities was a style that had not changed in a thousand years. It involved squat, mud-brick and clay-hued plaster buildings no more than two storeys high, which had the appearance of being half-melted into the ground. They were subject to constant repair but never knocked down or rebuilt. Their walls were thick, with the sills of their squarish windows measuring the length of a forearm in depth. Their corners were rounded and their threshold stones were worn into deep depressions from the passage of centuries of occupants. Each building held residences for many families with no connecting passages between them. Entrance was gained only through the roof above each home. The only door was a single entrance in each home to a shared central communal garden surrounding a well. Ladders led from the courtyard to the roof. When loved ones perished, they were buried within the thick walls and under the floors. Every home was crowded with ancestral bones. An example of this style was the village of
Rethik
.
Slavery
Slavery was common and tolerated by the continent's Malazan rulers. Slaves who escaped and were recaptured had their faces tattooed with a pattern that resembled shattered glass.
Climate
Summers in Seven Cities were hot and dry. With fall, nights became cooler and leaves turned rust-coloured.  Winters were mild and saw an increase in rain along the coasts.
Summer in the Seven Cities began with the
She'gai
, the hot wind.
In
Deadhouse Gates
In 1164
BS
, the Seven Cities natives launched the
Whirlwind
rebellion against the hated '
Mezla
' occupiers.
Fist
Coltaine
's
7th Army
, the only Malazan army stationed on the continent, attempted to march from far off
Hissar
to safety in Malazan-controlled
Aren
. They were decimated by constant attacks by the
Army of the Whirlwind
. Subsequently, the Malazan
14th Army
was sent under
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
as a punitive army to cut down the rebellion.
In
House of Chains
Osric
revealed that the subcontinent's name came from the unholy alliance between Dessimbelackis and the seven
Deragoth
during the time of the
First Empire
.
The Seven Holy Cities of Dessimbelackis' time were not the same cities given that designation at the time of the Malazan Empire.
Adjunct Tavore's 14th Army marched against the rebellious Army of the Whirlwind at their camp in
Raraku
.  Sha'ik was killed and her army routed at the
Battle of Raraku
. After the
Whirlwind Goddess
was destroyed, the Holy Desert was flooded and became an inland sea once more. The remnants of Sha'ik's army fled to
Y'Ghatan
under
Leoman
's leadership.
In
The Bonehunters
Telorast and Curdle
spoke of an ancient time long before the human First Empire or even the T'lan Imass when Seven Cities was covered by great forests of
Blackwood
and
Bloodwood
. The trees were revered by the
Tiste Edur
and feared by the
Eres
. The region was also home to vast cities and Shadow Temples.
(More information needed)
In
No Life Forsaken
(Information needed)
Trivia
Many of the locations in Seven Cities have names based on prehistoric dig sites that
Steven Erikson
pulled from one of his archaeology text books and moved around some of the letters. Examples include the
Dojal Hading Sea
,
Ubaryd
, and
Omari
.

Genabackis

======================================================================
PAGE: Shikimesh
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Shikimesh
======================================================================

'Shikimesh' by
Corporal Nobbs
Shikimesh
was a city on the
Seven Cities
continent that was destroyed by
Icarium
.
It was a desert city that cowered against limestone cliffs now blackened by smoke.  The narrow, dusty streets were littered with corpses and the shards of hundreds of shattered pots.  Only
Capemoths
,
rhizan lizards
, and
Bhoka'rala
resided there afterwards.
To the south lay old caravan camps, once visited by desert traders and merchants from distant cities, seeking the city's famous Redworm Silks.

PAGE: Sialk
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Sialk
======================================================================

Seven Cities detail
Seven Cities
Sialk
was a port city on the
Sahul Sea
on the east coast of
Seven Cities
.
It was located twenty leagues south of
Hissar
.
There was a small
Marine
garrison manning a stronghold and compound at the city harbour, which had its own jetty and three patrol craft.
In
Deadhouse Gates
Sialk was one of the first cities to fall during the
Whirlwind
Uprising. Some parts of the city went up in flames, and the Sialk Marines and thousands of Malazan nobles and their families were driven out of the city.
Trivia
The city is misspelled as "Silak" in the
Deadhouse Gates
glossary.

PAGE: Sogena
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Sogena
======================================================================

Genabackis
Sogena
was a former
Free City
on the River
Sogen
in northeastern
Genabackis
.
In
Orb Sceptre Throne
Sogena's existing tax system was one of many issues that the Warlord of the North,
Caladan Brood
, was asked to adjudicate. The issue concerning Sogena was whether or not the ex-Free City's tax system was unfair - as a number of concerned parties believed.
Trivia
Sogena appears as Suyema along the River Suyema on the
coloured version
of the Genabackis map.

PAGE: Sotka
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Sotka
======================================================================

Seven Cities
Sotka
was a city located in the north of the
Seven Cities
sub-continent on the shores of the
Kokakal Sea
.
Sotka Fork
seemed to be a branch of the
Sotka Road
coming from
Y'Ghatan
.
In
The Bonehunters
Sotka was the destination of the
Malaz 14th Army
for their rendezvous with Admiral
Nok
's fleet after the
Last Siege of Y'Ghatan
.
The army took the Sotka Fork to make the journey.
Ultimately, they circumvented the city and met Nok on the coast some thirteen leagues west.
During the disaster at Y'Ghatan,
Cotillion
rescued
Lostara Yil
and brought her to a hidden Temple of
Rashan
forty paces off the Sotka Road about a league and a half from the burning city.  After a few days, she joined
Fiddler
's band of stragglers as it followed the 14th Army along Sotka Road.

======================================================================
PAGE: Stratem
CATEGORIES: Continents
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Stratem
======================================================================

Unofficial Stratem Map
Created by D'rek, modified by Werthead
Malaz World Map
Stratem
[STRAT-em]
was a sub-continent, that together with the
Lands of Fist
, formed a continent generally referred to by the
Malazans
as
Korel
, although its actual name was unknown.  Stratem formed the southern portion of the continent while Fist formed the northern portion. They were separated by the
Aurgatt Range
.
Stratem became the homeland of the
Crimson Guard
after they left
Quon Tali
.
Regions
Haven Province
Notable locations
Canton's Landing
Cape of the Stone Army
Cursed Soldiers
Exile
- Crimson Guard fortress
Fortress Haven
- Crimson Guard fortress
Fortress Recluse
- Crimson Guard fortress
Grey Lands
Iron Citadel
- Crimson Guard fortress
North Bastion
- Crimson Guard fortress
Pine Fort
- Crimson Guard outpost
Thick
- Crimson Guard fortress
Thickton
Toll's City
- home of the
Chanters
In
Memories of Ice
Map of Korel and Stratem by
Joshua Butler
Esslee Monot (the Dubious)
wrote of an enormous
K'Chain Che'Malle
plaza on Stratem:
"
On the subcontinent of Stratem, beyond Korelri's south range, can be found a vast peninsula where even the gods do not tread. Reaching to each coast, encompassing an area of thousands of square leagues, stretches a vast plaza. Aye, dear readers, there is no other word for it. Fashion this in your mind: near-seamless flagstones, unmarred by age and of grey, almost black, stone. Rippled lines of dark dust, minuscule dunes heaped by the moaning winds, these are all that break the breathless monotony. Who laid such stones?
Should we give credence to
Gothos
's hoary tome, his glorious '
Folly
'? Should we attach a dread name to the makers of this plaza? If we must, then that name is K'Chain Che'Malle. Who, then, were the K'Chain Che'Malle? An Elder Race, or so Gothos tells. Extinct even before the rise of the
Jaghut
, the
T'lan Imass
, the
Forkrul Assail
.
Truth? Ah, if so, then these stones were laid down half a million - perhaps more - years ago. In the opinion of this chronicler, what utter nonsense.
"
―"My Endless Travels"
Esslee Monot (the Dubious)
In
Reaper's Gale
Onrack T'emlava
told
Quick Ben
and
Trull Sengar
of a concourse the size of a city-state on the southeast peninsula of Stratem where ritual wars had been fought among the K'Chain Che'Malle. The practise ended when the
Short-Tails
rebelled and the ritual form of war was abandoned.
In
Return of the Crimson Guard
By some unknown signal, the various Guard companies and blades strewn across the
Malazan world
were summoned to return and reunite at
Fortress Haven
on Stratem, ending the
Diaspora
. As
K'azz D'Avore
was still missing, overall command fell to
Skinner
who announced the time had come to march against their
Malazan
enemies.  New recruit,
Kyle
, stumbled upon a suspicious meeting between Skinner and
Cowl
leading to Skinner's murder of
Stoop
.  Kyle was falsely accused of the crime and fled from camp.
Badlands
,
Stalker
, and
Coots
volunteered to help track him down, but when they came upon Kyle three days later they instead helped him escape from
Mara
, one of the Guard mages.  The three
Lost brothers
had decided to desert the Guard and ivited Kyle to join them. The group made its way to
Canton's Landing
on Stratem's western shore where they attempted to steal a
boat
owned by
Traveller
and the
Thel Akai
,
Ereko
. The six reached an agreement to share the boat
Jacuruku
.
In
Stonewielder
After the
Battle of the Plains
and K'azz D'avore's return, the Crimson Guard resettled their old lands on Stratem.
Blues
became Lord Governor of
Haven Province
.
But when he received a report that
Iron Bars
was a prisoner on the
Stormwall
, Blues led
Fingers
,
Lazar
, and
Shell
on a rescue mission.  They crossed from Stratem over the
Iceback Range
to the
Lands of Fist
by foot, running afoul of the
Chase
, a
Jheck
war band.
In
Blood and Bone
Ardata
's servants,
Rutana
and
Nagal
, arrived by ship in
Haven
to request the Guard's aide against
Skinner
in Jacuruku.
In
Assail
Shimmer launched an expedition to find the missing
Cal-Brinn
and his
Blade
on
Assail
.
K'azz was not included as he was nowhere to be found. On the coast of Stratem, east of
Fortress Recluse
, K'azz summoned them to shore with a bonfire so he could accompany them.
In
Forge of the High Mage
The long-reaching racial memory of the
Thelomen
of the
Great Fenn Range
contained stories of an ancient war that had raged across the
Ice Wastes
of
Quon Tali
. It had involved a siege of one of the seven known
K'Chain Che'Malle
cities, also known as the Mountains that Move, by a coalition of races which had included Thelomen. A blast of energy released in the fighting had been responsible for creating the wasteland that remained today, much like another such mountain city had turned the land to glass on a great plain far south of Stratem.

======================================================================
PAGE: Strike
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Strike
======================================================================

Malazan Empire
Strike
was the largest city on
Strike Island
, the easternmost of the
Falari Isles
. It was located on the south shore of the Island. The city had immense, layered, seawall defences that were rivalled nowhere else in
Falar
but for the capital,
Cabil
.
History
According to the legends of the
Strike Islanders
, the more commonly known red- and gold-haired residents of the Falari Isles were actually invaders from across the other side of
Seeker's Deep
. Only the Strike islanders were the original residents of the islands, and their old maps of the island chain did not use the word "Falar".
These islanders may have been the
Walk people
.
In
Forge of the High Mage
As part of his plans to conquer Falar,
Malazan
Emperor
Kellanved
sent a fleet of freebooters to spread out and terrorise the local islands and settlements. Many captured cities and settlements to claim as their own fiefdoms. When the Falar's
Guiding Council of the Faith
sought to coordinate a unified response between the islands, Strike refused to lend any forces to free
Curaca
, citing a lack of numbers to both defend their own fortress and mount any offensive.

PAGE: Tanys
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Tanys
======================================================================

Northwest Genabackis
Tanys
was a busy port on the eastern coast of the
Malyn Sea
. It was variously named either a city or a town.
Tanys was described as resting on tiered ridges rising from the shore. It possessed at least one arched stone gateway which had a cobbled street leading from it with large three to four storey buildings lining it.
In
House of Chains
Tanys was where
Karsa Orlong
and
Torvald Nom
were transferred onto a ship to cross the
Malyn Sea
. Their captors,
Kindly
's 2nd Company of the
Ashok Regiment
crossed on another ship. The journey from Tanys across to
Malyntaeas
took four days and three nights.
Map gallery
Northwest Genabackis - Late Empire
Genabackis

======================================================================
PAGE: Taxila
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Taxila
======================================================================

Seven Cities
Taxila
was a city in the north of
Seven Cities
, located on the long
Maadil Peninsula
between the
Kokakal Sea
and
Maadil Sea
just north of the city of
Ashok
.  To Taxila's north lay the city of
Rang
.
The city's people were known as Taxilians and they had a distinctive tattoo style.
Something originating in or characteristic of Taxila was said to be Taxilii.
Notable natives
Taxilian
In
The Bonehunters
Admiral
Nok
was hoping to put in either at Taxila or Rang as he was unable to dock in any city east of Ashok on the Maadil Peninsula, and had been forced around it.
Taxila was home to the architect
Samar Dev
referred to as '
Taxilian
'.
Language
Since Taxilian spoke Taxilii Scholar's dialect, one can assume this language was also in use in Taxila, apart from
Malazan
and
Ehrlii
. Taxilian also mentioned a nearly extinct language called tribal
Rangala
, which was spoken by just himself and his grandfather's sister. One can presume, this language had something to do with the city of Rang, just north of Taxila itself.

PAGE: Tellick
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Tellick
======================================================================

Quon Tali
Tellick
was a city on the western coast of
Quon Tali
.  It was north of the city of
Quon Tali
and south of
Dass
.
In
Kellanved's Reach
In the early days of the formation of the
Malazan Empire
, Tellick belonged to
Nom Purge
. Tellick was located to the north of
Two-River Pass
, a pass which crossed some modest mountains which ran west to east, separating the southern lands of the
Quon Talians
from the northern territories of Quon Tali's ancient enemy,
Nom Purge
.
Two-River Fort
, located at the northernmost end of Two-River Pass, was the last fortress between the end of the pass and Tellick.

PAGE: Third Meckros city
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Third_Meckros_city
======================================================================

The
Third Meckros city
was one of the
Meckros
' floating island cities and home to twenty thousand residents. It was destroyed in 1159
BS
when mountains of ice rose unexpectedly from the depths of the sea. The largest such mountain appeared directly below the city breaking it to pieces like it was a raft of sticks, killing nearly everyone on board.
Notable residents
Withal
In
Midnight Tides
Withal
was the lone survivor of the city's destruction as he was pulled to safety by the
Crippled God
.
Speculations
The city may have been located west of the
Sepik Sea
near
Nemil
.
Admiral
Nok
cited old reports placing a Meckros city in that location.
Withal recalled how Meckros traders returned to the city from Nemil with
Bhok'arala
.
Notes and references

PAGE: Thol
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Thol
======================================================================

Korel,
aka
Lands of Fist
Thol
was a city on the southern shore of the
Fist Sea
amidst the
Trembling Range
, in the Kingdom of
Rool
.
Thol was considered a more desirable posting for government officials than
Banith
.
The nearby caves of the Ascetics, a network of tunnels, chambers, and temples in the Trembling Range, was one of the two most revered holy sites on the
Island of Fist
.

======================================================================
PAGE: Toll's City
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Toll's_City
======================================================================

Toll's City
was a small population centre surrounding a stone keep on
Stratem
. It was ruled by a "nasty mob of tyrants" known as the Chanters. At one point a fortified wall was built around the modest city, but building continued to expand outside the walls as villagers arrived from the surrounding countryside. The city had access to the sea at
Toll's Landing
.
A decade of warfare on Stratem resulted in the establishment of a permanent garrison in the city. The Chanters sought to end the violence and unify Stratem under their leadership with the help of the
Crimson Guard
. Half the Chanter treasury and a collection of ancient
idols
was collected as payment before the Crimson Guard abandoned the negotiations.
The court mage lived in a beehive apothecary sitting atop the city's lone hill.
In
The Lees of Laughter's End
Toll's City palace guard,
Sater
, conspired with gate sentries
Birds Mottle
,
Heck Urse
,
Gust Hubb
,
Sordid
, and
Wormlick
to steal the Chanter payment to the Crimson Guard. Fleeing on the
Suncurl
they were pursued by
Tiny Chanter
and others on the
Unreasoning Vengeance
.
Notes and references

PAGE: Traly
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Traly
======================================================================

Quon Tali
Traly
was a city on the main north-south trader road running through
Itko Kan
.
To the east were
Then
and
Buld
, and to the south was
Ijor
.
Notable Residents
Jadeen
In
Kellanved's Reach
Heboric
encountered Lady
Warin
's heavy wagon mired in mud outside Traly. After assisting the noblewoman's guards in pulling the wagon free, the priest joined their group as they headed north towards
Li Heng
. Four days north of the city the party was beset by assassins who eliminated Warin and her guards before Heboric called upon the power of his god to retaliate.

PAGE: Tramara
CATEGORIES: Cities

======================================================================

Seven Cities
Tramara
was one of several ancient ruined cities along the
Mersin River
on
Seven Cities
.  Like the others, it had practised intensive irrigation techniques to flood the plains for agriculture and cleared the forests to harvest lumber for ships.  Eventually the river choked itself with silt and the topsoil of the
Lato Odhan
disappeared making the area unable to sustain a large population for thousands of years.
In
The Bonehunters
While travelling through the area,
Icarium
recalled Tramara and the many other cities along the river.  He was shocked when
Mappo Runt
told him that most of the cities had long ago crumbled into ruin.  In fact, the amnesiac
Jhag
even failed to recall their last trip through the same region nearly eighty years earlier.

======================================================================
PAGE: Trate
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Trate
======================================================================

Map of Edur Lands and the North Lether frontier
Trate
was a port city in the
Kingdom of Lether
and the northernmost city of
Lether
.
It was surrounded by walls and protected by trebuchets and ballistae armed with hull-breaching quarrels.
A lighthouse overlooked the harbour front.
Tarancede Tower
, a seven-storey basalt watchtower, loomed over the southern end of Trate's harbour from an artificial, rocky island.
The city was home to the
Trate Legion
.
Before the region had been conquered and the city built by the Letherii, the land had once belonged to the
Fent
and
Nerek
.
Dissolute remnants of their cultures could still be found sold as curios in Trate's markets, including holy icons and relics, talking sticks of chiefs, medicine bags of
Shamans
, and Fent ancestor chests with the bones still in them.
Udinaas
had been a young
Indebted
sailor there in the year 1148 of
Burn's Sleep
before being taken as a slave by the
Tiste Edur
.
The city was known for its flower dancers.
Stalls in Trate's markets were known to occasionally find and sell the teeth and bones of
K'Chain Che'Malle
without knowing what they really were.
Notable citizens
Aranict
- midwife, then
Atri-Ceda
Buruk the Pale
- merchant house head
Hepar the Pleaser
- financier
Intaros
- merchant
Nekal Bara
- sorceress
Tharav the Hidden
- debt-holder
Udinaas
Notable locations
Chobor's Manse
Seal Street
Tarancede Tower
In
Midnight Tides
After taking revenge on the Letherii for poaching
Tusked seals
in
Tiste Edur
waters, Warlock King
Hannan Mosag
sent three vessels back to Trate as a warning. They were manned by
Shadow wraiths
and carried on the back of an immense
ocean spirit
. The spirit sent the ships crashing into the crowded docks along with a surge of water, fish, and crustaceans. The attack was witnessed in
Letheras
by
Ceda
Kuru Qan
through the obsidian tiles that ringed the top of the Tarancede Tower.
The Kingdom of Lether and the Tiste Edur were soon at war. At the start of hostilities, the
Cold Clay Battalion
was stationed in Trate in addition to the Trate Legion.
The battalion manned the waterside fortifications as a massive Edur fleet approached the harbour. Once again, the Edur sent the ocean spirit against the waterfront where it killed the sorcerers,
Nekal Bara
and
Arahathan
, and toppled the harbour's lighthouse.
Afterwards, the defenders' positions were swarmed by
Shadow wraiths
and the fleet landed and began unloading soldiers. At the same time, another Edur army led by Emperor
Rhulad Sengar
came from inland and took the city's North Gate. Once inside, the Edur proceeded to butcher every enemy soldier they could find. During the fighting,
Iron Bars
killed Rhulad to clear a path to safety for himself and
Seren Pedac
without suspecting his opponent was the Emperor of the Tiste Edur.

PAGE: Trebur
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Trebur
======================================================================

Seven Cities
Trebur
, the former City of Domes, was one of several ruined cities along the
Mersin River
on
Seven Cities
.  Like the others, they had practised intensive irrigation techniques to flood the plains for agriculture and cleared the forests to harvest lumber for ships.  Eventually the river choked itself with silt and the topsoil of the
Lato Odhan
disappeared making the area unable to sustain a large population for thousands of years.
In that time, the channel of the diminished Mersin River had migrated so far that its banks were a day's travel east of the city.
In
The Bonehunters
Icarium
vaguely recalled having visited Trebur and was shocked when
Mappo Runt
told him that most of the cities along the river had long ago crumbled into ruin.  The amnesiac
Jhag
remembered only that he had once done something important in the city and resolved to travel there.  Mappo remembered making the same trip to Trebur nearly eighty years earlier when Icarium's memory was even more fragmented.  He feared what the Jhag might recall during their return.

======================================================================
PAGE: Ubaryd
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Ubaryd
======================================================================

Seven Cities
Area between
Hissar
and
Ubaryd
Ubaryd
[OOB-ar-id]
was one of the
Holy Cities
of
Seven Cities
. It was located on the south coast of the subcontinent on the
Dojal Hading Sea
.
It was a two month journey by land from
Sekal
.
Before coming under the reign of the
Malazan Empire
, it was an independent city-state ruled by a
Holy Falah'd
. The last Holy Falah'd of Ubaryd was slain by
Dassem Ultor
during the Seven Cities campaigns.
The city's Holy Champion had been
Yrgell
.
The city's palace was decorated with coral marble.
The people were known as the Ubari.
In
Deadhouse Gates
During the
Whirlwind
Uprising the Malazan fleet at Ubaryd was forced to flee and tens of thousands of refugees were driven northeast into the
Ubaryd Odhan
.
Fist
Coltaine
, fleeing
Hissar
and
Kamist Reloe
's Army of the Apocalypse, attempted to bring his
Chain of Dogs
to safe harbour in Ubaryd before discovering that the city had already fallen.
At least three Ubari legions joined the Army of the Apocalypse against Coltaine at the
Battle of Gelor Ridge
.
In
House of Chains
While
Adjunct
Tavore Paran
's
Malaz 14th Army
marched overland to confront the
Army of the Whirlwind
,
Admiral
Nok
was tasked with recapturing the continent's port cities.
By the time the Adjunct reached
Vathar Crossing
, Nok had already taken Ubaryd. From a butte above the river, the Adjunct could see Nok's ships filling the city's harbour.  Once secured, the city would be used to resupply her army.
In
Night of Knives
Temper
recalled how he and
Point
of
Dassem's First Sword
had followed Dassem Ultor into the Palace of Ubaryd's Holy Falah'd after the fall of the city to the Malazans. Finding her bound and tortured by three
Claws
, Dassem granted her a mercy killing despite the assassins' protest.
Trivia
Ubaryd was one of many Seven Cities location names based on prehistoric dig sites that
Steven Erikson
pulled from one of his archaeology text books and moved around some of the letters.

======================================================================
PAGE: Ugarat
CATEGORIES: Cities
URL: https://malazan.fandom.com/wiki/Ugarat
======================================================================

Map of Seven Cities
Ugarat by
Corporal Nobbs
Ugarat
was one of
Seven Cities
' holy cities. It was located on the
Ugarat Odhan
at the center of the continent. The
River Ugarat
that passed through the city continued on to
Sarpachiya
and
Nahal
before reaching the
Clatar Sea
. The city of
Kayhum
was upriver to the northeast.
A
Malazan
-built imperial road connected the city to
Lato Revae
.
A broad stone bridge crossed the broad River Ugarat within sight of the city's northern walls.
The ancient fortress of
Moraval Keep
lay on the opposite side of the river from the city.
The city had an underground sewer system and Malazan aqueducts that brought water into the city. Hot water was brought into homes via pipes.
The people who lived there were referred to as "Ugari".
Notable residents
Avower
, royal torturer
Enqura
, former Holy Falah'd
Falah'd of Ugarat
, current young Falah'd
Febryl
Inashan
, city guard captain
Samar Dev
Notable locations
Inn of the Wood
Moraval Keep
Trosfalhadan Street
History
Over a thousand years ago, Ugarat had been at the centre of scores of caravan routes between a dozen great cities. But desertification led to the collapse of all these cities but the two on the banks of the River Ugarat, Ugarat and Kayhum.
At the time of the
Malazan Empire
's conquest of Seven Cities, Ugarat and its tributary cities had been undergoing a renaissance under
Holy Falah'd
Enqura
. The city had supported eleven great schools of learning which were relearning the lost knowledge of the ancient
First Empire
. This ended when
Dassem Ultor
seized the city.
Ugarat by
Shadaan
But Enqura prepared for the city's fall, directing
Febryl
to confiscate the schools' hundred thousand scrolls and bound volumes a week before the
Mezla
arrival. These were burned in a great pyre within the city's coliseum. At the same time, the teachers and scholars were arrested. Many threw themselves upon the fires in anguish as their treasures burned. The rest were crucified and their bodies thrown into pits outside the city walls along with smashed relics of the First Empire. When the Malazans took over they were infuriated to discover the schools empty.
During the Malazan invasion, many Ugari fled the city to find refuge with the
Anibar
tribe in the
Jhag Odhan
. The Malazans followed and slew them while bringing no harm to the Anibar. King
Iskar Jarak
(as the Anibar knew him) advised the Anibar to flee before others came to destroy them. The Anibar called the period of the Malazan invasion the Time of Great Slaying.
During the time of Malazan rule the Empire banned the use of torture by the Royal
Avowers
and established a
Garrison
.
When the sub-continent rebelled in the
Whirlwind
uprising, the Malazan garrison fled across the river to Moraval Keep.
In
House of Chains
Karsa Orlong
tested his newly acquired steed,
Havok
, within sight of Ugarat's northern walls.  He raced a score of the city's horsemen to reach the river's bridge a full fifty strides ahead of his pursuers.
In
The Bonehunters
Karsa returned to Ugarat, this time accompanied by the scholar,
Samar Dev
, whom he had found injured in the Ugarat Odhan. The
Teblor
hoped the scholar could help him enter the city unnoticed so he could obtain supplies, but the plan failed immediately. When a city guardsman attempted to confiscate the
Deragoth
heads Karsa carried as trophies, Karsa knocked him unconscious. Samar Dev was able to convince
Captain
Inashan
to halt further violence and Karsa agreed to bring terms of peace to the Malazan garrison besieged inside
Moraval Keep
.
The Teblor discovered the entire garrison had been massacred by a
K'Chain Nah'ruk
that had been mistakenly freed from its tomb within the keep.
Samar Dev was asked to examine the creature by the Falah'd and conducted an extensive study of its remains.
Karsa proved difficult and disrespectful during his stay in the city. The Falah'd was only too happy to provide the Teblor with supplies if it meant he left the city immediately.
In
Toll the Hounds
During her time away with Karsa Orlong, Samar Dev grew to miss the creature comforts of her home city. She was startled when
Tulas Shorn
spoke the native tongue of Ugari.
Notes and references
